🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1ANA pattern in SLE?Homogeneous (dsDNA, Histones) — Most common; Speckled also common (ENA)
2ANA Centromere pattern — associated disease?Limited SSc (CREST), Primary Biliary Cholangitis
3c-ANCA vs p-ANCA — target antigens?c-ANCA = PR3 (Proteinase 3), p-ANCA = MPO (Myeloperoxidase)
4c-ANCA positive — most likely diagnosis?GPA (Granulomatosis with Polyangiitis) — 90% specificity
5p-ANCA positive — differential?MPA (70%), EGPA (40%), Drug-induced, UC, PSC, AIH
6. Anti-Sm significance?100% Specific for SLE (30% sensitive) — Diagnostic if positive
7Anti-Centromere — associated disease?Limited SSc (CREST), Primary Biliary Cholangitis
8RF vs Anti-CCP in RA?RF: 85% Spec, Prognostic; Anti-CCP: >95% Spec, Prognostic for Erosions
9Low C3 + Low C4 + Low CH50 — mechanism?Classical Pathway Consumption (SLE, Cryoglobulinaemia, Post-strep GN)
10Cryoglobulin Type II — association?HCV (90%), Lymphoproliferative disorders

🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"ANA Positive = SLE"NO. ANA positive in 5-20% healthy, Sjögren's, SSc, MCTD, RA, Drug-induced, Infections, Malignancy.
"ANA Negative = No SLE"NO. 2-5% SLE are ANA-negative (Anti-dsDNA rogue, Technical failure, Early disease).
"c-ANCA = GPA 100%"NO. 90% specificity; 10% false + (Drugs, CF, Other); 5-10% GPA are ANCA-negative.
"p-ANCA = MPA Only"NO. p-ANCA = MPO-ANCA = MPA (70%), EGPA (40%), Drug-induced, UC, PSC, AIH.
"RF = RA"NO. RF in Sjögren's, SLE, Cryoglobulinaemia, Chronic Infections, Healthy Elderly (5-10%).
"Anti-CCP = RA Only"NO. High specificity (>95%), but also in Pre-RA, PsA, SSc, CVID; High titre = Erosive RA.
"Low C3 + Low C4 = Only SLE"NO. Also Cryoglobulinaemia, Post-Streptococcal GN, Infective Endocarditis, Subacute Bacterial Endocarditis.
"p-ANCA = MPA Only"NO. EGPA (40%), Drug-induced, UC, PSC, AIH, Atypical p-ANCA in IBD.
"ANA Negative = No Autoimmune Disease"NO. Seronegative SLE (2-5%), Seronegative RA, ANCA Vasculitis, Adult Stills, IBD.
"ENA Panel = All Autoantibodies"NO. Standard ENA = 10-15 antigens; Missing: dsDNA (Separate), ANCA (Separate), aPL (Separate), RF (Separate), HLA (Separate).
Mnemonic: AUTOIMMUNE DIAGNOSTICS
ANA Patterns: Homogeneous (dsDNA/SLE), Speckled (ENA), Centromere (Ltd SSc), Nucleolar (SSc), Cytoplasmic (Jo-1)
Universal Screening: ANA — High Sensitivity, Low Specificity → If +ve → ENA Panel
Targeted ENA: Sm (SLE), RNP (MCTD), Ro/La (Sjögren), Jo-1 (Antisynthetase), Scl-70 (SSc), Centromere (Ltd SSc), RNA Pol III (SSc+SRC)
ONCogene vs TSG: Not relevant here (Just mnemonic filler)
Immunoglobulins: RF (IgM Anti-IgG), Anti-CCP (Citrullinated Peptide)
Mimicry & Epitope Spreading: Diagnosis Clues
MHC: HLA-B27 (AS), DR4 (RA), DQ2/8 (Celiac), DR3/4 (T1D), B51 (Behcet)
Unusual ANCA: c-ANCA/PR3=GPA, p-ANCA/MPO=MPA/EGPA, Atypical=UC/PSC/AIH
Neutrophil ANCA: c-ANCA=PR3, p-ANCA=MPO — IIF Pattern + ELISA Confirmation
ENA Panel: Sm (SLE), RNP (MCTD), Ro/La (Sjögren), Jo-1 (Antisyn), Scl-70 (SSc), Centromere (CREST), RNA Pol III (SRC), Mi-2/TIF1γ/MDA5 (DM)
Complement: Low C3+C4 (Classical/SLE), Low C3 Only (Alt Path/C3GN), C4 Only (Classical Def/HAE)
RF vs CCP: RF 85% Spec, CCP >95% Spec, CCP Prognostic for Erosion
Y (Cryoglobulins): Type I (Monoclonal/WM), Type II (Mono IgM + Poly IgG/HCV), Type III (Poly/Poly/HCV)
Antiphospholipid: LA (dRVVT), aCL, β2-GPI — 2x ≥12w
Neutrophil Alkaline Phosphatase: Not relevant (Mnemonic filler)
Organ Specific: Anti-TSHR (Graves), Anti-AChR (MG), Anti-GBM (Goodpasture), Anti-DSG (Pemphigus)
Serology Algorithm: ANA+ → ENA; ANCA+ → PR3/MPO ELISA; RF/CCP → RA; aPL → LA/aCL/β2-GPI
Diagnosis: Clinical + Serology + Histology + Imaging
Immunofluorescence: HEp-2 ANA, Neutrophil ANCA, DIF (Skin/Kidney), IIF (Autoantibody Titration)
Specificity vs Sensitivity: CCP > RF, dsDNA > ANA, Sm > dsDNA, Centromere > ANA
Test Selection: Clinical Suspicion → Targeted Panel → Reflex Testing → Genetic if Negative

💬 Exam Answer Modes

FormatPromptKey Points
Long Essay"Describe the approach to interpreting a positive ANA result in a patient with suspected systemic autoimmune disease."ANA patterns, ENA panel, Pattern-specific associations, Clinical correlation, False positives, Algorithm
Short Note"ANCA testing in vasculitis."IIF patterns (c-ANCA/p-ANCA), PR3/MPO ELISA, GPA/MPA/EGPA differentiation, Atypical patterns, Negative ANCA ≠ Exclusion
Viva"Patient with positive ANA (1:320 Speckled), Anti-Ro+, Anti-La+, Schirmer's 3mm. Diagnosis?"Sjögren's Syndrome — ANA Speckled, Anti-Ro/La+, Sicca symptoms → EULAR 2016 criteria met.
Ward Round"Patient with haemoptysis, haematuria, c-ANCA positive. Diagnosis and confirmatory test?"GPA (c-ANCA/PR3) — Confirm with PR3-ANCA ELISA; Biopsy for granulomas (ENT/Lung/Kidney).
Last-Night"ANA: Homog/Speck/Centromere/Nucleolar. ENA: Sm(SLE), RNP(MCTD), Ro/La(Sjögren), Scl-70(SSc), Centromere(CREST), RNA Pol III(SRC). ANCA: c-ANCA=PR3=GPA, p-ANCA=MPO=MPA/EGPA. RF 85%Spec, CCP>95%Spec. Comp: Low C3+C4=Classical(SLE), Low C3=AltPath, Low C4=ClassicalDef/HAE. Cryo: I(Mono), II(Mixed/HCV), III(Poly). aPL: LA+dRVVT, aCL, β2GPI. RF/CCP: CCP>95%Spec."Compressed.

📌 Summary

  • ANA: Screening test — Patterns: Homogeneous (dsDNA/SLE), Speckled (ENA), Centromere (CREST/SSc), Nucleolar (SSc), Cytoplasmic (Jo-1)
  • ENA Panel: Sm (SLE, 100% Spec), RNP (MCTD), Ro/La (Sjögren's), Scl-70 (Diffuse SSc), Centromere (Limited SSc), RNA Pol III (SSc+SRC), Jo-1 (Anti-synthetase)
  • ANCA: c-ANCA/PR3 = GPA (90% Spec), p-ANCA/MPO = MPA/EGPA, Atypical = UC/PSC/AIH/Drugs
  • RF vs Anti-CCP: RF 85% Spec, Prognostic; Anti-CCP >95% Spec, Prognostic for erosions
  • Complement: Low C3+C4 = Classical Consumption (SLE, Cryo); Low C3 only = Alternative Pathway; Low C4 only = Classical Deficiency/HAE
  • Cryoglobulins: Type I (Monoclonal), II (Mixed, HCV 90%), III (Polyclonal)
  • aPL: LA (dRVVT), aCL, β2-GPI — 2 occasions ≥12w; APS = Thrombosis + Pregnancy Morbidity + aPL
  • Diagnostic Algorithms: ANA+ → ENA; ANCA+ → PR3/MPO ELISA → Clinical Correlation; Clinical Context Essential

❓ MCQs (10)

  1. ANA pattern in SLE — most common?

A. Centromere B. Nucleolar C. Homogeneous D. Cytoplasmic

Answer: C. Homogeneous (dsDNA, Histones) is most common in SLE.

  1. Anti-Sm antibody — significance?

A. Sensitive for SLE B. 100% Specific for SLE C. Sjögren's marker D. SSc marker

Answer: B. Anti-Sm = 100% specific for SLE (30% sensitive).

  1. c-ANCA target antigen?

A. MPO B. PR3 (Proteinase 3) C. Lactoferrin D. Cathepsin G

Answer: B. PR3 (Proteinase 3).

  1. p-ANCA positive — most likely diagnosis?

A. GPA B. MPA or EGPA C. SLE D. Sjögren's

Answer: B. p-ANCA/MPO = MPA (70%) or EGPA (40%).

  1. Anti-Centromere antibody — associated disease?

A. Diffuse SSc B. Limited SSc (CREST) C. SLE D. Sjögren's

Answer: B. Limited SSc (CREST), Primary Biliary Cholangitis.

  1. Anti-CCP vs RF — specificity in RA?

A. RF > Anti-CCP B. Equal C. Anti-CCP >95% Spec, RF 85% Spec D. Both 100%

Answer: C. Anti-CCP >95% Specific, RF 85% Specific.

  1. Low C3 + Low C4 + Low CH50 — mechanism?

A. Alternative pathway B. Classical pathway consumption C. Terminal pathway D. C1-INH deficiency

Answer: B. Classical pathway consumption (SLE, Cryoglobulinaemia).

  1. Cryoglobulin Type II — composition?

A. Monoclonal IgM + Polyclonal IgG B. Polyclonal IgM + Polyclonal IgG C. Monoclonal IgG D. Monoclonal IgM

Answer: A. Monoclonal IgM (κ) + Polyclonal IgG (HCV 90%).

  1. Antiphospholipid antibody testing — required?

A. LA only B. aCL only C. LA (dRVVT) + aCL + β2-GPI (2 occasions ≥12w) D. β2-GPI only

Answer: C. LA (dRVVT) + aCL IgG/IgM + Anti-β2-GPI IgG/IgM — 2 occasions ≥12 weeks.

  1. Low C3, Normal C4 — pathway?

A. Classical B. Alternative C. Lectin D. Terminal

Answer: B. Alternative pathway (C3 Nephritic Factor, C3 Glomerulopathy).

📋 SBAs (10)

  1. 30F with malar rash, arthritis, anti-dsDNA+, low C3/C4. ANA pattern likely?

A. Centromere B. Homogeneous C. Nucleolar D. Speckled

Answer: B. Homogeneous = dsDNA, Histones (SLE).

  1. 55M with RPGN, c-ANCA positive. Confirmatory test?

A. MPO-ANCA B. PR3-ANCA ELISA C. ANA D. Cryoglobulins

Answer: B. PR3-ANCA ELISA confirms GPA.

  1. Patient with recurrent DVT, livedo reticularis, positive LA (dRVVT). aCL negative. Diagnosis?

A. APS B. SLE C. TTP D. HIT

Answer: A. APS — LA positive (dRVVT) meets laboratory criteria.

  1. 50F with Raynaud's, calcinosis, telangiectasia. Anti-centromere+. Diagnosis?

A. Diffuse SSc B. Limited SSc (CREST) C. SLE D. MCTD

Answer: B. Anti-Centromere = Limited SSc (CREST).

  1. Patient with recurrent DVT, positive aCL IgG, negative LA. Repeat aCL in 12w positive. Diagnosis?

A. APS B. AT deficiency C. Protein C deficiency D. Antithrombin deficiency

Answer: A. APS — aCL positive on 2 occasions ≥12w apart meets laboratory criteria.

▸ 4.4 Hypersensitivity & Allergy 1
▸ 4.4.01 Hypersensitivity Allergy

Parent Topic: Clinical Immunology MOC → Chapter 4 Hierarchy

Status: full-fcps-mrcp-note

Priority: ⭐⭐⭐ HIGHEST (FCPS/MRCP — Gell & Coombs Classification, Anaphylaxis, Asthma, Drug Allergy, Allergy Testing)

Source: Davidson 24th Ed Ch 4; BSACI/WAO Guidelines; NICE/BSR; FCPS/MRCP/MRCPCH Syllabus

1. 1. 🎯 Learning Objectives

  • [ ] Apply Gell & Coombs Classification — Type I-IV (and V) Hypersensitivity mechanisms, Examples
  • [ ] Manage Anaphylaxis — Algorithm (Adrenaline IM, IV Fluids, Oxygen, Adjuncts), Biphasic, Tryptase
  • [ ] Diagnose & Manage Asthma — Phenotypes/Endotypes, Stepwise Management (BTS/SIGN), Biologics
  • [ ] Manage Allergic Rhinitis/Conjunctivitis — ARIA Guidelines, Immunotherapy (SCIT/SLIT)
  • [ ] Diagnose Food Allergy — IgE vs Non-IgE, Component-Resolved Diagnostics, Oral Food Challenge
  • [ ] Manage Drug Hypersensitivity — SJS/TEN/DRESS/AGEP, HLA Associations, Cross-Reactivity, Desensitisation
  • [ ] Apply Allergy Diagnostics — SPT, sIgE, Component-Resolved Diagnostics, BAT, Patch Testing, Oral Food Challenge
  • [ ] Answer viva: "Anaphylaxis Algorithm" and "SJS vs TEN vs DRESS" and "Component-Resolved Diagnostics"

2. 2. 🧠 Core Concept: Gell & Coombs Classification

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Hypersensitivity Reactions
↓
Type I: IgE-Mediated (Immediate)
Type II: Antibody-Mediated (Cytotoxic)
Type III: Immune Complex-Mediated
Type IV: T-Cell Mediated (Delayed)
Type V: Stimulatory (Autoantibody)
↓
Anaphylaxis, Asthma, Allergic Rhinitis, Food Allergy, Atopic Dermatitis
AIHA, ITP, Goodpasture, Graves, Myasthenia Gravis, Drug-Induced
SLE, Serum Sickness, Vasculitis, Arthus, Farmer's Lung
Contact Dermatitis, TB Test, Drug Hypersensitivity (SJS/TEN/DRESS), TB, Granulomas
Graves (TSHR Stimulating), MG (AChR Block), Pemphigus (AChR Modulating)

3. 3. ️⃣ Type I Hypersensitivity (IgE-Mediated / Immediate)

1. Pathophysiology

PhaseMechanism
SensitisationAllergen → DC → Th2 → IL-4/IL-13 → B cell class switch → IgE → Binds FcεRI on Mast cells/Basophils
EffectorRe-exposure → Allergen cross-links IgE-FcεRI → Degranulation (Histamine, Tryptase, PGD2, LTC4, PAF) + Cytokines (IL-4, IL-5, IL-13)
Late Phase (4-12h)Eosinophils, Th2 cells, Basophils → Tissue damage, Remodelling

2. Key Mediators

MediatorSourceEffects
HistamineMast cells, BasophilsVasodilation, ↑ Vascular permeability, Bronchoconstriction, Pruritus
TryptaseMast cellsBiomarker (Peak 1-2h, Half-life 2h), Fibrosis, Airway remodelling
PGD2Mast cellsBronchoconstriction, Vasodilation, Flushing
LTC4, LTD4, LTE4 (CysLTs)Mast cells, EosinophilsPotent bronchoconstriction, Mucus, Vascular permeability
PAFMast cells, Basophils, PlateletsPlatelet activation, Vascular permeability, Bronchoconstriction
IL-4, IL-5, IL-13Th2, ILC2, Mast cellsIL-5 → Eosinophilia, IL-13 → IgE, Airway remodelling, IL-4 → IgE switching

4. 4. ️⃣ Anaphylaxis

1. Diagnostic Criteria (WAO/RS)

Anaphylaxis HIGHLY LIKELY if ANY 1 of 3:

  1. Acute onset (mins-hours) + Skin/Mucosal (Urticaria, Angioedema, Flushing) + Respiratory (Wheeze, Stridor, Dyspnoea) OR Cardiovascular (Hypotension, Syncope, Tachycardia)
  2. Acute onset + 2+ Systems: Skin + Respiratory + Cardiovascular + GI
  3. Acute hypotension after known allergen exposure

2. Emergency Algorithm (RCUK/WAO/RCUK 2021)

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Recognise Anaphylaxis
↓
Call for Help / Code Blue
↓
**ADRENALINE IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh**
↓
Response?
↓
**Repeat Adrenaline IM q5min** Max 3 doses
Position: Supine + Legs Raised (If Breathless: Semi-recumbent)
↓
**O2 High Flow** (15L/min)
**IV Fluid Challenge** 500-1000ml Crystalloid Bolus
**Chlorphenamine 10mg IV** (Adjunct)
**Hydrocortisone 200mg IV** (Adjunct — Late effect)
**Salbutamol Neb** (If Bronchospasm)
↓
Continuous Monitoring ECG, SpO2, BP, RR, Peak Flow
↓
Observe 6-12h (Biphasic Reaction Risk 20%)

3. Adrenaline Dosing

Age/WeightIM Dose (1:1000)
Adult0.5 mg (0.5 mL)
Child >12y / >50kg0.5 mg (0.5 mL)
Child 6-12y / 25-50kg0.3 mg (0.3 mL)
Child 6m-6y / 7.5-25kg0.15 mg (0.15 mL)
Infant <6m / <7.5kg0.1 mg (0.1 mL)
Key: Adrenaline IM is FIRST-LINE and LIFE-SAVING — No contraindication in anaphylaxis. Repeat q5min if no improvement.

4. Biphasic Reaction

FeatureDetail
Incidence1-20% (Higher if delayed adrenaline)
Timing1-72h after initial resolution (Peak 3-10h)
Risk FactorsDelayed adrenaline, Severe initial reaction, Inadequate initial dose, No observation
ManagementObserve 6-12h post-resolution; Adrenaline available

5. Serum Tryptase

TimingInterpretation
BaselinePre-reaction (if known)
Peak (1-2h post-onset)>11.4 ng/mL OR >2x Baseline + 1.2x = Supports anaphylaxis
24hReturns to baseline (Half-life ~2h)
Elevated BaselineMastocytosis, Clonal mast cell disease

5. 5. ️⃣ Bronchial Asthma

1. Phenotypes & Endotypes

PhenotypeKey FeaturesEndotypeKey Biomarkers
Allergic (Early-onset)Atopy, Childhood onset, RHType 2 HighFeNO >25 ppb, Eos >150/μL, IgE↑, Periostin
Non-Allergic (Late-onset)Non-atopic, Adult onset, ObesityType 2 Low / Non-Type 2Neutrophilia, Low FeNO, Obesity
EosinophilicSputum Eos >3%Type 2 HighBlood Eos >300/μL, FeNO >50 ppb
NeutrophilicSputum Neut >60%Non-Type 2 / Th17Neutrophilia, IL-17, IL-8
Aspirin-Exacerbated Respiratory Disease (AERD)Asthma + Nasal Polyps + NSAID SensitivityCysLT OverproductionHigh CysLTs, Eosinophilia
Obese AsthmaBMI >30, Late-onset, Poor controlMixed / Non-Type 2Low FeNO, Low Eos, Metabolic syndrome

2. BTS/SIGN 2024 Stepwise Management (Adults)

StepTreatmentDose/Details
Step 1SABA PRN (Salbutamol 100-200mcg)As needed
Step 2Low-dose ICS (Beclomethasone 200-400mcg/d) + SABA PRNRegular ICS — Start if symptoms >2/wk or night waking
Step 3Low-dose ICS + LABA (Fixed combination)Add LABA if not controlled on ICS alone
Step 4Medium-dose ICS + LABAIncrease ICS to medium dose (Beclo 800mcg/d)
Step 5High-dose ICS + LABA + Add-onLAMA (Tiotropium), LTRA (Montelukast), Theophylline
Step 6High-dose ICS + LABA + BiologicAnti-IL5 (Mepolizumab/Reslizumab/Benralizumab), Anti-IL4Rα (Dupilumab), Anti-TSLP (Tezepelumab), Anti-IgE (Omalizumab)
Step Down: Review q3m, Step down if controlled 3m
SMART/MART: Single Maintenance and Reliever Therapy (Budesonide/Formoterol, Beclo/Formoterol) — Preferred for Steps 3-5

3. Severe Asthma Biologics (GINA 2024 / NICE)

BiologicTargetIndicationDose
OmalizumabAnti-IgESevere Allergic Asthma (IgE 30-1500 IU/mL, Sensitisation)75-600mg SC q2-4w
Mepolizumab / ReslizumabAnti-IL-5Severe Eosinophilic Asthma (Blood Eos ≥150-300/μL)100mg SC q4w / 3mg/kg IV q4w
BenralizumabAnti-IL-5RαSevere Eosinophilic Asthma (Eos ≥300/μL)30mg SC q4w ×3, then q8w
DupilumabAnti-IL-4RαSevere Type 2 High (Eos ≥150; FeNO ≥25)600mg SC loading → 300mg q2w
TezepelumabAnti-TSLPSevere Asthma (Broad Type 2)210mg SC q4w

4. Acute Severe Asthma (Life-Threatening)

FeatureThreshold
PEF<33% Best/Predicted
SpO₂<92% on Air
PaCO₂Normal/Raised (Normal = Impending Respiratory Failure)
Silent Chest—
Cyanosis / Exhaustion / Confusion—
TreatmentDose
O₂ (Target SpO₂ 94-98%)High Flow (15L)
Salbutamol Neb5mg q15-30min (Continuous if severe)
Ipratropium Neb500mcg q20-30min (Add to Salbutamol)
IV Magnesium Sulphate2g IV over 20min (Single dose)
IV Hydrocortisone100mg (or Pred 40-50mg PO)
IV AminophyllineOnly if Life-Threatening (5mg/kg loading, 0.5-0.7mg/kg/h)
EscalationICU, IV Salbutamol Infusion, NIV/Intubation, ECMO

6. 6. ️⃣ Allergic Rhinitis & Conjunctivitis (ARIA Guidelines)

1. Classification

DurationIntermittentPersistent
SeverityMild (Normal sleep, No impairment)Mild
Moderate-Severe (≥1: Sleep disturbance, Impairment, Troublesome)Moderate-Severe

2. Management (ARIA 2020)

StepIntermittentPersistent
MildOral/Intranasal H1-Antihistamine PRNIntranasal Corticosteroid (INCS) + H1-Antihistamine PRN
Moderate-SevereINCS + H1-Antihistamine (Regular)INCS + H1-Antihistamine (Regular) + LTRA (Montelukast) if ASTHMA
RefractoryINCS + H1 + LTRA OR Short Oral SteroidINCS + H1 + LTRA OR Immunotherapy

3. Allergen Immunotherapy (AIT)

TypeIndicationProtocol
SCIT (Subcutaneous)Perennial/Seasonal IgE-mediatedBuild-up (Weekly × 3-6m) → Maintenance (Monthly × 3-5y)
SLIT (Sublingual)Perennial/SeasonalDaily drops/tablet (3-5y)
IndicationsIgE-mediated, Mod-Severe, Pharmacotherapy failure, Allergen avoidance impossible
ContraindicationsUncontrolled Asthma, Severe CVD, Immunodeficiency, β-blockers, Pregnancy (Initiation)

7. 7. ️⃣ Food Allergy

1. Classification

TypeMechanismOnsetExamples
IgE-MediatedType IMinutes-2hPeanut, Egg, Milk, Fish, Shellfish, Tree nuts, Soy, Wheat
Non-IgE MediatedType IV (T-cell)Hours-DaysFPIES (Food Protein-Induced Enterocolitis), FPIAP (Proctocolitis), EoE (Eosinophilic Oesophagitis)
MixedIgE + Non-IgEVariableEoE, Some Atopic Dermatitis

2. Diagnosis

TestUtility
HistoryCornerstone — Timing, Reproducibility, Co-factors (Exercise, Alcohol, NSAIDs)
SPTSensitivity 90%, PPV ~50% (Wheal ≥3mm)
sIgESensitivity 90%, Component-resolved useful
Component-Resolved Diagnostics (CRD)Identifies specific proteins (Ara h 2 for Peanut, Ara h 8 for Cross-reactivity)
Basophil Activation Test (BAT)Functional, High specificity, Research/Refractory
Oral Food Challenge (OFC)Gold Standard — Double-blind, Placebo-controlled (DBPCFC)

3. Component-Resolved Diagnostics (CRD) — Peanut Example

ComponentClinical Significance
Ara h 1, 2, 3Primary Sensitisers — High risk systemic reaction
Ara h 8PR-10 (Bet v 1 Homolog) — Cross-reactivity (Birch pollen), Usually mild
Ara h 9LTP — Severe reactions, Heat stable, Mediterranean

4. Management

StepAction
AvoidanceStrict allergen avoidance, Label reading, Adrenaline Auto-Injector (AAI) — 2 devices at all times
Acute ReactionAdrenaline IM (Anaphylaxis) → Antihistamine (If mild)
ImmunotherapyOIT (Oral Immunotherapy) — Palforzia (Peanut), EPIT (Epicutaneous — Viaskin)
PreventionEarly Introduction (LEAP Study: Peanut 4-11m → ↓ Allergy 80%)

8. 8. ️⃣ Drug Hypersensitivity

1. Classification (Pichler)

TypeMechanismTimingExamples
Type I (IgE)Immediate<1hPenicillins, NMBA, Latex
Type II (Cytotoxic)Antibody-dependent5-10dPenicillin-induced AIHA, Heparin-Induced Thrombocytopenia (HIT)
Type IIIImmune Complex1-3wSerum Sickness, Serum Sickness-Like Reaction (SSR)
Type IVa (Th1)Macrophage activation2-6wDRESS, AGEP, TB Test
Type IVb (Th2)Eosinophil recruitment2-6wDRESS, SJS/TEN, AGEP, Maculopapular Exanthema (MPE)
Type IVc (CTL)Cytotoxic T cells2-6wSJS/TEN, DRESS, Fixed Drug Eruption
Type IVd (Th17)Neutrophil recruitment2-6wAGEP, Pustular Psoriasis

2. Severe Cutaneous Adverse Reactions (SCARs)

SyndromeTime to OnsetKey FeaturesMortalityManagement
SJS (Stevens-Johnson Syndrome)7-21d<10% BSA Detachment, Mucosal ≥2 sites, Target lesions, Fever~5%Stop Drug, IVIG 2-3g/kg or Plasma Exchange, Supportive
TEN (Toxic Epidermal Necrolysis)7-21d>30% BSA Detachment, Mucosal ≥2 sites, Nikolsky+, Sepsis Risk25-30%Immediate ICU, Supportive, IVIG 2-3g/kg / PLEX, Ciclosporin, Etanercept
SJS/TEN Overlap7-21d10-30% BSA Detachment10-15%Same as TEN
DRESS2-8wFever, Rash, Eosinophilia, Lymphadenopathy, Visceral (Liver > Kidney), HHV-6 Reactivation10%Stop Drug, Steroid (Pred 1mg/kg), IVIG if severe
AGEP1-5dAcute Febrile Neutrophilic Pustulosis, Neutrophilia, Fever, No Mucosal<5%Stop Drug, Topical Steroids, Self-limiting

3. SCORTEN (TEN Severity Score)

ParameterScore 1 Point
Age >40y
Malignancy
Heart Rate >120
BSA Detached >10%
Serum Urea >10mmol/L
Serum Bicarbonate <20mmol/L
Glucose >14mmol/L
ScoreMortality
0-13.2%
212.1%
335.3%
458.3%
≥590%

4. Drug Cross-Reactivity (Key)

Drug ClassCross-Reactivity
PenicillinsCarbapenems (1%), Cephalosporins (1-2% 1st/2nd gen, <1% 3rd/4th gen)
SulfonamidesSulfonamide cross-reactivity (Sulfamethoxazole, Sulfasalazine, Dapsone)
NSAIDsCross-reactivity within class (Aspirin → Ibuprofen/Naproxen)
ARBs/ACEiLow cross-reactivity
StatinsLow cross-reactivity

5. Desensitisation

ScenarioProtocol
Penicillin (IgE)Rapid (4-6h) or Slow (Days) — Incremental doses under monitoring
Aspirin (AERD)Incremental Oral Aspirin (Start 20mg, Double q1-2h → 650mg)
Carboplatin/Oxaliplatin12-step Protocol (Pre-med: Dexamethasone, Antihistamine, H2-blocker)
AllopurinolNot Recommended (High failure) — Avoid, Switch to Febuxostat

6. HLA-Drug Hypersensitivity Associations (High-Yield)

HLA AlleleDrugReactionPopulationScreening
HLA-B*57:01AbacavirHypersensitivity (fever, rash, GI, respiratory)All (NPV >98%)Mandatory pre-prescription
HLA-B*15:02CarbamazepineSJS/TENHan Chinese, Thai, Malaysian, IndianMandatory pre-prescription (Asian ancestry)
HLA-B*58:01AllopurinolSJS/TEN/DRESSHan Chinese, Korean, Thai, EuropeanStrongly recommended (all ancestries)
HLA-A*31:01CarbamazepineSJS/TEN/DRESS/MaculopapularEuropean, JapaneseRecommended
HLA-DRB1*07:01FlucloxacillinDILI (Drug-induced liver injury)EuropeanConsider
HLA-B*57:01FlucloxacillinDILIEuropeanConsider

9. 9. ️⃣ Allergy Testing

1. Skin Prick Testing (SPT)

FeatureDetail
PrincipleAllergen → Mast cell degranulation → Wheal/Flare
PositiveWheal ≥3mm (vs Negative Control)
ControlsPositive: Histamine 10mg/mL; Negative: Saline/Glycerol
ContraindicationsSevere anaphylaxis risk, Severe uncontrolled asthma, Antihistamines (Stop 48-72h), Tricyclics, Severe Dermographism
Sensitivity/Specificity90%/90% (Aeroallergens), Food: Sens 90%, PPV 50%

2. Intradermal Testing (IDT)

FeatureDetail
PrincipleAllergen injected intradermally (0.02-0.05 mL) → Wheal/Flare
IndicationsDrug allergy (Penicillin, Venom), Aeroallergens when SPT negative but high suspicion
PositiveWheal ≥5mm (erythema) at 15-20 min
SensitivityHigher than SPT (esp. drug/venom), but ↓ specificity
RiskHigher anaphylaxis risk than SPT — Resuscitation equipment required
Concentrations1:100 to 1:1000 of SPT concentration

3. Patch Testing (Type IV)

FeatureDetail
Sensitivity90% (Aeroallergens)
Specificity90% (Depends on allergen)
ISAC (ImmunoCAP ISAC)112 Components on microarray — Component-resolved
AdvantagesNo antihistamine stop, Quantitative, Component-resolved

4. Component-Resolved Diagnostics (CRD)

ApplicationBenefit
Peanut (Ara h 1/2/3 vs Ara h 8/9)Ara h 1/2/3 = Primary = High Risk; Ara h 8/9 = Cross-reactivity (Bet v 1, LTP) = Lower Risk
Hazelnut (Cor a 1 vs 9/14)Cor a 1 = PR-10 (Birch), Cor a 9/14 = Storage (High Risk)
Apple (Mal d 1 vs 3)Mal d 1 = PR-10 (Birch) = Mild; Mal d 3 = LTP = Severe
Wheat (Tri a 19/ω-5 Gliadin)ω-5 Gliadin = Severe (WDEIA)

5. Basophil Activation Test (BAT)

FeatureDetail
PrincipleAllergen → Basophil CD63/CD203c upregulation (Flow Cytometry)
Sensitivity/Specificity90-95% / 90-95% (Superior to sIgE for some foods/drugs)
IndicationsFood/Drug Allergy (sIgE/SPT discordant), Venom, CRD Equivocal

6. Patch Testing (Type IV)

FeatureDetail
AllergensBaseline Series (Fragrance, Nickel, Cobalt, Potassium Dichromate, Balsam of Peru, Parabens, Formaldehyde, etc.)
ReadingDay 2 (48h) + Day 3-4 (72-96h)
Grading (ICDRG)+ (Erythema), ++ (Papules/Infiltration), +++ (Vesicles)
Irritant vs AllergicIrritant: Fades by Day 3; Allergic: Persists/Increases

7. Oral Food Challenge (OFC)

TypeProtocol
OpenKnows allergen — Clinical practice
Single-BlindPatient blinded
Double-Blind, Placebo-Controlled (DBPCFC)Gold Standard — Research, Diagnostic uncertainty

10. 10. ⚡ FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
Hypersensitivity TypesType I: IgE, Mast cells, Anaphylaxis/Asthma; Type II: Antibody-mediated (AIHA, ITP); Type III: Immune complexes (SLE, Serum Sickness); Type IV: T-cell (Contact, TB, Drug); Type V: Stimulatory (Graves)
AnaphylaxisAdrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh — Repeat q5min; Obs 6-12h (Biphasic); Tryptase 1-2h peak
AsthmaBTS/SIGN Steps 1-6; SMART/MART (Buda/Form, Beclo/Form); Biologics: Anti-IgE, Anti-IL5/5R, Anti-IL4Rα, Anti-TSLP
Allergic RhinitisARIA: Intermittent/Persistent × Mild/Mod-Severe → INCS ± H1 ± LTRA; AIT (SCIT/SLIT) 3-5y
Food AllergyIgE (Minutes-2h) vs Non-IgE (Hours-Days); CRD (Ara h 1/2/3 = Risk, Ara h 8/9 = Cross-reactivity); OFC = Gold Standard
Drug HypersensitivitySJS/TEN/DRESS/AGEP — SCORTEN (TEN); Stop Drug → ICU/Supportive/IVIG/PLEX; Desensitisation (Penicillin, Aspirin, Carboplatin)
Allergy TestingSPT (Wheal ≥3mm); sIgE (ImmunoCAP); CRD (Ara h 1/2/3 = Risk, 8/9 = Cross-reactivity); BAT (CD63/CD203c); Patch (Type IV); OFC = Gold Standard
AnaphylaxisAdrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh — q5min; Observation 6-12h; Tryptase 1-2h peak

11. 11. 🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1Anaphylaxis — first-line treatment?Adrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh — Repeat q5min if no improvement; No contraindication
2Anaphylaxis — biphasic reaction risk factors?Delayed adrenaline, Severe initial reaction, Inadequate initial dose, No observation period
3.Asthma — stepwise management?BTS/SIGN 1-6: SABA → Low ICS → Low ICS+LABA → Med ICS+LABA → High ICS+LABA+Add-on → Biologics (Anti-IgE, IL-5, IL-4R, TSLP)
4.SJS vs TEN — difference?SJS: <10% BSA detachment; TEN: >30% BSA detachment; Overlap 10-30%; SCORTEN for prognosis
5.DRESS vs SJS/TEN — key differences?DRESS: 2-8w onset, Fever, Rash, Eosinophilia, Lymphadenopathy, Visceral (Liver), HHV-6; SJS/TEN: 7-21d, Mucosal ≥2 sites, BSA Detachment, Nikolsky+
5.Anaphylaxis — adrenaline dose?0.5mg IM (1:1000) anterolateral thigh; Repeat q5min
6.Biphasic anaphylaxis — observation period?6-12 hours post-resolution
6.Serum tryptase — timing?Peak 1-2h post-onset; >11.4 ng/mL or >2x baseline + 1.2x supports anaphylaxis
7.Asthma biologics — anti-IL5 indication?Severe Eosinophilic Asthma (Blood Eos ≥150-300/μL)
8.Food allergy — component-resolved diagnostics?Ara h 1/2/3 = Primary sensitisation (High risk); Ara h 8/9 = Cross-reactivity (Bet v 1/LTP)
8.SJS vs TEN — BSA detachment?SJS <10%, SJS/TEN 10-30%, TEN >30%
9.SJS vs DRESS — key difference?DRESS: 2-8w onset, Fever, Eosinophilia, Visceral (Liver), HHV-6; SJS/TEN: 7-21d, Mucosal ≥2, Nikolsky+
10.Penicillin allergy — desensitisation protocol?Rapid (4-6h) or Slow (Days) — Incremental doses under monitoring; Not for SJS/TEN history

12. 12. 🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"Anaphylaxis = Only with hives"NO. Can present WITHOUT Skin (Cardiovascular/Respiratory only) — Still anaphylaxis!
"Adrenaline = Contraindicated in Heart Disease"NO. NO Absolute Contraindication in Anaphylaxis — Life-saving!
"SPT = Diagnostic for Food Allergy"NO. SPT/sIgE = Sensitisation, Not Allergy; OFC = Gold Standard for diagnosis
"SJS = Mild, TEN = Severe"NO. Spectrum: SJS (<10% BSA), SJS/TEN Overlap (10-30%), TEN (>30%); Mortality: SJS 5%, SJS/TEN 10%, TEN 25-30%
"DRESS = Just Rash"NO. Multisystem: Fever, Rash, Eosinophilia, Lymphadenopathy, Hepatitis (ALT↑), Nephritis, HHV-6 Reactivation
"All Drug Rashes = Allergy"NO. Morbilliform (MPE) = Most common, Benign; SCARs (SJS/TEN/DRESS/AGEP) = Severe
"AGEP = Pustular Psoriasis"NO. AGEP: Acute Febrile Neutrophilic Pustulosis, Drug-induced, Neutrophilia, Self-limiting
"SPT Positive = Allergy"NO. Sensitisation ≠ Clinical Allergy; Need History + OFC (Gold Standard)
"All Penicillin Allergic = Avoid All β-lactams"NO. Cross-reactivity Low (Carbapenems 1%, 3rd/4th Gen Cephalosporins <1%); Assess individually
"Adrenaline IV = Better than IM"NO. IM Preferred (Rapid absorption, Safer); IV only in Cardiac Arrest or Refractory Shock with monitoring
Mnemonic: HYPERSENSITIVITY ALLERGY ESSENTIALS
Hypersensitivity Types: I (IgE/Immediate), II (Ab-Mediated), III (IC-Mediated), IV (T-Cell), V (Stimulatory)
Y (Anaphylaxis): Adrenaline IM 0.5mg 1:1000 → q5min; O2, IV Fluids, Chlorphenamine, Hydrocortisone, Salbutamol; Observe 6-12h (Biphasic)
P (Types): I (IgE/Anaphylaxis/Asthma), II (Ab-Med/AIHA/ITP), III (IC/SLE/Serum Sickness), IV (T-Cell/Contact/TB/Drug), V (Stimulatory/Graves)
Endotypes Asthma: T2-High (Eos, FeNO, IgE) vs T2-Low (Neutrophilic, Obese) — Biologics Target T2
R (Rhinitis): ARIA: Intermittent/Persistent × Mild/Mod-Sev → INCS ± H1 ± LTRA → AIT (SCIT/SLIT 3-5y)
S (Skin Tests): SPT (Wheal ≥3mm, Stop Antihist 48-72h), sIgE (ImmunoCAP), CRD (Ara h 1/2/3=Risk, 8/9=Cross), BAT (CD63/CD203c), Patch (Type IV, Day 48/72h), OFC=Gold Standard
Hypersensitivity Types: I (IgE), II (Ab-Med Cytotoxic), III (IC-Med), IV (T-Cell), V (Stimulatory)
SCARs: SJS (<10% BSA), SJS/TEN (10-30%), TEN (>30%); SCORTEN (Age>40, Malig, HR>120, BSA>10%, Urea>10, Bicarb<20, Gluc>14)
E DRESS: 2-8w, Fever, Rash, Eos, Lymphadeno, Viscera (Liver), HHV-6
N AGEP: 1-5d, Neutrophilic Pustules, Neutrophilia, Self-Limiting
Studies: OFC=Gold Standard, SPT (Wheal≥3mm, Stop AntiH 48-72h), sIgE (ImmunoCAP), CRD (Ara h 1/2/3=Risk, 8/9=Cross), BAT (CD63/CD203c), Patch (Day 48/72h)
Immune: Type I (IgE), II (Ab), III (IC), IV (T-Cell)
Treatment: Anaphylaxis = Adrenaline IM 0.5mg 1:1000, Asthma (BTS/SIGN Steps), Rhinitis (ARIA), Drug Desens (Penicillin, Aspirin)
IgE: High Affinity FcεRI on Mast/Baso, Degranulation (Histamine, Tryptase, PGD2, CysLTs)
V (Viva): Anaphylaxis=Adrenaline; Asthma=BTS Steps; SJS/TEN=BSA%; DRESS=Liver/HHV-6; CRD=Ara h 2/3 Risk
V (Viva): SJS<10%, SJS/TEN 10-30%, TEN>30%; SCORTEN; DRESS=Liver/HHV-6; CRD=Ara h 1/2/3=Risk
Exam: Anaphylaxis=Adrenaline IM; Asthma=BTS Steps; SJS/TEN=BSA%; DRESS=Liver; CRD=Ara h 1/2/3

16. 16. 💬 Exam Answer Modes

FormatPromptKey Points
Long Essay"Describe the classification, clinical features, and management of anaphylaxis."Gell & Coombs Type I, WAO Criteria, Adrenaline IM Algorithm, Biphasic, Tryptase, Adjuncts, Observation
Short Note"SJS vs TEN vs DRESS — differentiation."BSA Detachment thresholds, Onset timing, Mucosal involvement, Systemic features, SCORTEN, Management
Viva"Patient on allopurinol develops fever, rash, eosinophilia, hepatitis. Diagnosis and management?"DRESS (Drug Reaction with Eosinophilia and Systemic Symptoms) — Stop drug, Steroids, IVIG if severe, HHV-6 reactivation, RegiSCAR
Ward Round"Patient with peanut allergy given peanut butter. Develops wheeze, lip swelling, hypotension. Immediate management?"Anaphylaxis — Adrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh, Oxygen, IV Fluids, Chlorphenamine, Hydrocortisone, Observe 6-12h
Last-Night"Types: I(IgE/Anaphylaxis), II(Ab/AIHA/ITP), III(IC/SLE/Serum Sickness), IV(T-Cell/Contact/TB/Drug), V(Stimulatory/Graves). Anaphylaxis: Adrenaline IM 0.5mg 1:1000 anterolateral thigh q5min → O2/IV Fluids/Chlorphenamine/Hydrocortisone → Observe 6-12h Biphasic → Tryptase 1-2h peak. Asthma: BTS Steps 1-6 → SMART/MART → Biologics (Anti-IgE/IL5/IL-4R/TSLP). SJS/TEN/DRESS: BSA<10%/10-30%/>30%, DRESS=Liver/HHV-6/2-8w, SCORTEN. Allergy: SPT/sIgE/CRD/BAT/OFC. Desensitisation: Penicillin/Aspirin/Carboplatin."Compressed.

17. 17. 📌 Summary

  • Gell & Coombs: Type I (IgE/Anaphylaxis), Type II (Ab-mediated), Type III (IC/SLE), Type IV (T-cell/Contact/Drug), Type V (Stimulatory/Graves)
  • Anaphylaxis: Adrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) Anterolateral Thigh — FIRST-LINE, NO CONTRAINDICATION; Repeat q5min; Observe 6-12h (Biphasic); Tryptase 1-2h peak
  • Asthma: BTS/SIGN Steps 1-6, SMART/MART (Buda/Form, Beclo/Form), Biologics (Anti-IgE, Anti-IL5, Anti-IL4R, Anti-TSLP)
  • Allergic Rhinitis: ARIA (Intermittent/Persistent × Mild/Mod-Sev); INCS ± H1 ± LTRA; AIT (SCIT/SLIT 3-5y)
  • Food Allergy: IgE (Min-2h) vs Non-IgE (Hrs-Days); CRD (Ara h 1/2/3 = Risk, 8/9 = Cross); OFC = Gold Standard
  • Drug Hypersensitivity: SCARs — SJS/TEN/DRESS/AGEP; SCORTEN (TEN), RegiSCAR (DRESS); Desensitisation (Penicillin, Aspirin, Carboplatin)
  • Allergy Testing: SPT (Wheal ≥3mm, Stop AntiH 48-72h); sIgE (ImmunoCAP); CRD (Ara h 1/2/3 = Risk, 8/9 = Cross); BAT (CD63/CD203c); Patch (Day 48/72h); OFC = Gold Standard
  • Drug Desensitisation: Penicillin (Rapid/Slow), Aspirin (AERD), Carboplatin (12-step), Allopurinol (Avoid)

18. 18. ❓ MCQs (10)

  1. First-line treatment for anaphylaxis:

A. IV Hydrocortisone B. Adrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) C. Chlorphenamine D. Salbutamol Nebuliser

Answer: B. Adrenaline IM 0.5mg (1:1000) anterolateral thigh — FIRST-LINE, NO contraindication.

  1. Biphasic anaphylaxis — observation period?

A. 1 hour B. 6-12 hours C. 24 hours D. 48 hours

Answer: B. Observe 6-12 hours post-resolution (Biphasic peak 3-10h).

  1. Serum tryptase — optimal timing for anaphylaxis confirmation?

A. Immediately B. 1-2 hours post-onset C. 6 hours D. 24 hours

Answer: B. Peak at 1-2 hours; half-life ~2h; >11.4 ng/mL or >2x baseline supports diagnosis.

  1. SJS vs TEN — key differentiator?

A. Mucosal involvement B. BSA Detachment (<10% SJS, >30% TEN) C. Fever D. Drug cause

Answer: B. BSA Detachment: SJS <10%, SJS/TEN 10-30%, TEN >30%.

  1. DRESS vs SJS/TEN — key distinguishing feature?

A. Mucosal involvement B. Fever, Eosinophilia, Visceral (Liver), HHV-6 Reactivation C. Nikolsky sign D. Drug cause

Answer: B. DRESS = Fever, Eosinophilia, Lymphadenopathy, Visceral (Liver), HHV-6 Reactivation (2-8w onset).

  1. Asthma biologics — Anti-IL5 (Mepolizumab) indication?

A. All severe asthma B. Severe Eosinophilic Asthma (Blood Eos ≥150-300/μL) C. Allergic asthma only D. Exercise-induced asthma

Answer: B. Severe Eosinophilic Asthma (Blood Eos ≥150-300/μL).

  1. Food allergy — Component-Resolved Diagnostics for Peanut:

A. Ara h 8 = High risk B. Ara h 1/2/3 = Primary sensitisers (High Risk); Ara h 8/9 = Cross-reactivity C. Ara h 9 = Primary D. All equal

Answer: B. Ara h 1/2/3 = Primary sensitisation (High risk); Ara h 8/9 = Cross-reactivity (Bet v 1/LTP).

  1. Penicillin allergy — desensitisation approach?

A. Not possible B. Rapid (4-6h) or Slow (Days) — Incremental doses under monitoring C. Single dose challenge D. Only with antihistamine cover

Answer: B. Rapid (4-6h) or Slow (Days) — Incremental doses under monitoring.

  1. Skin Prick Test — positive criteria?

A. Wheal ≥2mm B. Wheal ≥3mm (vs Negative Control) C. Flare ≥10mm D. Any wheal

Answer: B. Wheal ≥3mm larger than negative control.

  1. Oral Food Challenge — gold standard for?

A. Aeroallergy B. Food Allergy Diagnosis C. Drug Allergy D. Contact Dermatitis

Answer: B. Double-Blind Placebo-Controlled Food Challenge (DBPCFC) = Gold Standard for Food Allergy.

  1. Drug desensitisation — when indicated?

A. All drug allergies B. No Alternative Drug Available (e.g., Penicillin in Syphilis, Aspirin in AERD, Carboplatin in Ovarian Cancer) C. Only for IgE-mediated D. Never

Answer: B. When no safe alternative exists (Penicillin in Syphilis, Aspirin in AERD, Carboplatin in Ovarian Cancer).

19. 19. 📋 SBAs (10)

  1. 25F with anaphylaxis to peanut. Adrenaline IM 0.5mg given. Still wheezy, BP 80/50 after 5min. Next step?

A. Repeat Adrenaline IM 0.5mg B. IV Hydrocortisone C. IV Chlorphenamine D. Salbutamol Neb

Answer: A. Repeat Adrenaline IM 0.5mg q5min if no improvement.

  1. Patient on carbamazepine develops fever, rash, eosinophilia 3.5x10⁹/L, ALT 300, HHV-6 PCR+. Diagnosis?

A. SJS B. TEN C. DRESS D. AGEP

Answer: C. DRESS (Drug Reaction with Eosinophilia and Systemic Symptoms) — Fever, Rash, Eosinophilia, Hepatitis, HHV-6 reactivation.

  1. Asthma patient on Step 4 (Medium-dose ICS/LABA) still uncontrolled. Blood Eos 400/μL, FeNO 45ppb. Add-on?

A. Tiotropium B. Montelukast C. Mepolizumab (Anti-IL5) D. Omalizumab

Answer: C. Anti-IL5 (Mepolizumab/Reslizumab/Benralizumab) for Severe Eosinophilic Asthma (Eos ≥150-300/μL).

  1. Child with peanut allergy — Ara h 2 positive, Ara h 8 negative. Risk?

A. Low (Cross-reactivity) B. High (Primary Sensitisation) C. Moderate D. None

Answer: B. Ara h 2 = Primary Sensitiser = High Risk for Systemic Reaction.

  1. Patient on allopurinol develops fever, rash, eosinophilia 2x10⁹/L, pustules. Onset Day 3. Diagnosis?

A. SJS B. DRESS C. AGEP (Acute Generalised Exanthematous Pustulosis) D. TEN

Answer: C. AGEP — Acute onset (1-5d), Neutrophilic Pustules, Neutrophilia, Self-limiting.

🧠 Core Concept: Transplant Immunology

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Transplant Immunology
↓
HLA System Class I (A,B,C) / Class II (DR, DQ, DP)
Allorecognition Direct / Indirect / Semi-direct
Rejection Mechanisms Hyperacute / Acute Cellular / Antibody-Mediated / Chronic
Immunosuppression Induction / Maintenance / Rescue
HSCT Indications / Conditioning / GvHD / Reconstitution
Monitoring DSA / dd-cfDNA / Gene Expression / Biopsy (Banff)

1️⃣ HLA System

HLA Structure & Expression

ClassGenesExpressionFunction
Class IHLA-A, HLA-B, HLA-CAll nucleated cellsPresent endogenous peptides (8-10aa) to CD8+ T cells
Class IIHLA-DR, HLA-DQ, HLA-DPAPCs (DC, B cells, Macrophages, Thymic epithelium)Present exogenous peptides (13-25aa) to CD4+ T cells
Class IIIComplement (C2, C4, Factor B), TNF, LTA, HSP70VariousInflammation, Complement

HLA Nomenclature

FormatExampleMeaning
AlleleHLA-A*02:01HLA-A locus, allele group 02, specific protein 01
SerologicalHLA-A2Historical serological equivalent
HaplotypeHLA-A1, B8, DR3Set of alleles inherited together

HLA Matching in Transplantation

Transplant TypeMatching Priority
KidneyHLA-A, -B, -DR (6/6 ideal) — HLA-DR most important
LiverHLA-A, -B, -DR (Less critical, HLA matching less critical)
Heart/LungHLA-A, -B, -DR (Size/urgency prioritized)
PancreasHLA-A, -B, -DR (Similar to kidney, DR priority) — Often simultaneous kidney-pancreas (SPK)
IntestineHLA-A, -B, -DR (Less studied, high rejection risk) — Multivisceral often
HSCTHLA-A, -B, -C, -DRB1, -DQB1 (10/10 ideal) — High-resolution

Epitope Matching (Eplet Mismatch)

ConceptDescription
EpletPolymorphic amino acid configuration on HLA surface recognised by antibodies
Eplet Mismatch LoadNumber of mismatched eplets — Better predictor of DSA development than antigen mismatch
Permissible MismatchesEplets shared between donor/recipient → Acceptable

2️⃣ Allorecognition Pathways

PathwayMechanismKey FeaturesRelevance
DirectRecipient T cells recognise Intact Donor HLA on Donor APCs (Passenger leukocytes)Strong, Early (Peaks 1-2w), Dominates Acute Cellular RejectionDominant in early ACR
IndirectRecipient T cells recognise Processed Donor HLA Peptides on Recipient APCsWeaker, Chronic, Drives Chronic Rejection, Antibody-Mediated RejectionDominant in Chronic Rejection, AMR
Semi-DirectRecipient APCs acquire Intact Donor HLA (Exosomes, Trogocytosis) → Present to Recipient T cellsIntermediate, Contributes to both ACR and AMREmerging role

3️⃣ Rejection — Classification & Mechanisms

Banff Classification (Kidney) — Major Categories

TypeMechanismTimingKey Features
HyperacutePre-formed DSA → Complement activation → Immediate thrombosis, NecrosisMinutes-HoursGraft loss (Irreversible), CDC-XM Positive
Acute Cellular Rejection (ACR)Host T cells → Donor HLA (Direct > Indirect)Days-Weeks (Peak 1-3m)Banff t-Score (t1/t2/t3), Tubulitis (t), Interstitial Inflammation (i)
Antibody-Mediated Rejection (AMR)Donor-Specific Antibodies (DSA) → Complement Activation, Endothelial InjuryHours-MonthsC4d+ (C4d2/3), DSA+, Microvascular Inflammation (g/ptc), Endothelial Changes
Chronic Active AMRDSA + Chronic Endothelial InjuryMonths-YearsTransplant Glomerulopathy (cg), Peritubular Capillary Basement Membrane Multilayering
Chronic Active T-Cell MediatedPersistent T-cell AlloresponseMonths-YearsArterial Intimal Fibrosis (cv), Interstitial Fibrosis/Tubular Atrophy (IF/TA)

Banff Scoring (Kidney) — Key Lesions

LesionScoreSignificance
t (Tubulitis)t0 (0), t1 (1-4), t2 (5-10), t3 (>10)ACR Severity
i (Interstitial Inflammation)i0 (0%), i1 (10-25%), i2 (26-50%), i3 (>50%)ACR Severity
g (Glomerulitis)g0-g3AMR Activity
ptc (Peritubular Capillaritis)ptc0-ptc3AMR Activity
cg (Transplant Glomerulopathy)cg0-cg3Chronic AMR
cv (Vascular Intimal Fibrosis)cv0-cv3Chronic Vascular Rejection
C4d (Peritubular Capillaries)C4d0 (Negative), C4d1 (Minimal), C4d2 (Focal), C4d3 (Diffuse)AMR Marker

Rejection — Diagnosis & Treatment

Rejection TypeDiagnosisFirst-Line Treatment
HyperacuteCDC-XM Positive, Immediate graft failureNone (Graft loss) — Prevention: CDC-XM Negative
ACR (TCMR)Biopsy (Banff t/i scores), DSA NegativePulse Methylpred 500-1000mg x3-5d → Optimise Maintenance IS
AMRDSA+, C4d+, Microvascular Inflammation (g+ptc)Pulse Methylpred, PLEX/IA (5-7 exchanges), IVIG 2g/kg, Rituximab (Anti-CD20), Eculizumab (Refractory)
Chronic AMRDSA+, cg>0, ptcml, C4d+Optimise IS, PLEX/IVIG, Bortezomib (Plasma cells), Eculizumab (Refractory)
Chronic TCMRcv>0, IF/TAOptimise IS, Belatacept (CNI-sparing), Control BP/Lipids

4️⃣ Immunosuppression

Induction Therapy (Peri-Transplant)

AgentMechanismIndicationKey Points
BasiliximabAnti-CD25 (IL-2Rα)Standard risk (Low immunologic risk)Non-depleting, Low infection risk
Alemtuzumab (Campath)Anti-CD52 (Pan-lymphocyte depletion)High immunologic risk (Re-transplant, PRA>80%, ABOi)Profound Lymphodepletion, ↑ Infection/CMV
ATG (Thymoglobulin)Anti-Thymocyte Globulin (Polyclonal)High Risk, Delayed Graft FunctionProfound Depletion, Cytokine Release Syndrome
RituximabAnti-CD20 (B-cell depletion)ABOi, HLAi, AMR ProphylaxisB-cell depletion, IgG decline

Maintenance Immunosuppression (Triple Therapy Standard)

Drug ClassAgentsMechanismKey MonitoringKey Toxicities
CNI (Calcineurin Inhibitors)Tacrolimus (Tac), Cyclosporine (CsA)Inhibit Calcineurin → ↓ IL-2 TranscriptionTrough Levels (C0), Renal Function, Glucose, Lipids, K⁺, Mg²⁺Nephrotoxicity, Neurotoxicity, HTN, Diabetes, Hyperkalaemia
mTOR InhibitorsSirolimus (SRL), Everolimus (EVR)Inhibit mTOR → ↓ Protein Synthesis, Cell Cycle ArrestTrough Levels, Lipids, CBC, Wound HealingHyperlipidaemia, Thrombocytopenia, Impaired Wound Healing, Proteinuria, Pneumonitis
AntimetabolitesMycophenolate (MMF/MPA/EC-MPS), Azathioprine (AZA)Inhibit IMPDH (MMF) / Purine Synthesis (AZA)CBC, LFT, Renal, TPMT (AZA)GI (Diarrhoea/Nausea), Leukopenia, Teratogenicity (MMF)
SteroidsPrednisolone, MethylprednisoloneGenomic/Non-genomic Anti-inflammatoryBP, Glucose, Bone, Eyes, Weight, CataractsInfection, Diabetes, Osteoporosis, Avascular Necrosis, Cataracts
Costimulation BlockerBelatacept (CTLA-4-Ig)Blocks CD28-CD80/86 → No Co-stimulationMonthly IV, Renal Function, EBV IgG (Pre-req)PTLD (EBV-), Infection, Infusion Reactions

CNI Minimisation / Belatacept Conversion

ScenarioStrategy
CNI NephrotoxicityCNI → Belatacept (BENEFIT/EXTEND Trials), or CNI → mTOR (Conversion)
CNI MinimisationLow-dose CNI + MMF + Belatacept (Viking Trial)
CNI-FreeBelatacept + MMF + Steroid (EBV+ Recipients Only)

Tacrolimus vs Cyclosporine

FeatureTacrolimusCyclosporine
PotencyMore Potent (2-4x)Less Potent
NephrotoxicitySimilarSimilar
NeurotoxicityTremor, Headache, Insomnia, PRESLess
Diabetes (PTDM)Higher IncidenceLower
HyperlipidaemiaLowerHigher
HypertensionLowerHigher
CosmeticAlopecia, HirsutismGingival Hyperplasia, Hirsutism
LevelsC0 (Trough)C0 or C2 (2h Post-dose)

5️⃣ Haematopoietic Stem Cell Transplantation (HSCT)

Indications

CategoryExamples
MalignantAML, ALL, Lymphoma (HL, NHL), Myeloma, MDS, MPN, CML (TKI Failure)
Non-MalignantSCID, Thalassaemia Major, Sickle Cell, Aplastic Anaemia, HLH, Inborn Errors of Metabolism, Autoimmune (Refractory)

Donor Sources (Hierarchy)

SourceMatchAdvantagesDisadvantages
MSD (Matched Sibling Donor)10/10 HLABest OS, Lowest GvHDOnly 25-30% have MSD
MUD (Matched Unrelated Donor)10/10 or 9/10Large Registries (Anthony Nolan, DKMS)Slightly Higher GvHD
HaploidenticalHaplo (5/10)Universal Donor (Parents, Siblings, Children)PTCy Required (Post-Transplant Cyclophosphamide)
Cord Blood4-6/6Rapid Availability, Lower GvHDLow Cell Dose, Delayed Engraftment, Higher Relapse
Mismatched Unrelated9/10, 8/10Alternative if no MUDHigher GvHD

Conditioning Regimens

TypeRegimenIndicationKey Features
Myeloablative (MAC)Busulfan/Cyclophosphamide, TBI/CyclophosphamideYoung, Fit, AML/ALLFull Ablation, High Toxicity, Faster Engraftment
Reduced Intensity (RIC)Fludarabine + Melphalan/Busulfan (Low Dose)Older, Comorbid, AML in CRLess Toxicity, Relies on GvL Effect, Slower Engraftment
Non-Myeloablative (NMA)Fludarabine + Low-Dose TBI (2Gy)Elderly, ComorbidMinimal Toxicity, Relies Entirely on GvL

Graft-versus-Host Disease (GvHD)

TypeTimingKey FeaturesGrading
Acute GvHD (aGvHD)<100 Days (Classical), Late aGvHD (100d-1y)Skin (Rash), GI (Diarrhoea, Nausea), Liver (Bilirubin ↑), Lung (Bronchiolitis Obliterans — Late)MAGIC/Glucksberg (Skin 1-4, GI 1-4, Liver 1-4) → Overall Grade I-IV
Chronic GvHD (cGvHD)>100 DaysSclerotic (Scleroderma-like), Sicca, Bronchiolitis Obliterans, Fasciitis, Ocular, AutoimmunityNIH Consensus 2014/2020 (Mild/Moderate/Severe)

GvHD Prophylaxis

RegimenComponentsKey Points
Standard (MSD/MUD)CNI (Tac) + Antimetabolite (MMF/MTX) + SteroidMTX (Days 1,3,6,11) or MMF
HaploidenticalPTCy (Post-Transplant Cyclophosphamide 50mg/kg Day +3, +4) + Tac + MMFStandard of Care, Reduces GvHD without increasing relapse
Cord BloodCNI + MMF/MTXHigher GVHD Risk
ATG/SerotherapyATG (Thymoglobulin) or AlemtuzumabIn RIC, Haplo, T-cell Depleted Grafts

GvHD Treatment

SeverityAcute GvHDChronic GvHD
Mild (Grade I)Topical Steroids (Skin), Budesonide/Beclomethasone (GI)Topical/Steroids, Tacrolimus (Systemic low-dose)
Moderate (Grade II)Systemic Steroids (Pred 1-2mg/kg)Systemic Steroids (Pred 0.5-1mg/kg), Ecp (ECP)
Severe (Grade III-IV)High-Dose Steroids (MP 2mg/kg), Add Antithymocyte Globulin (ATG) / Ruxolitinib (JAK1/2i)High-Dose Steroids, Ruxolitinib (JAK1/2i), Ecp, Ibrutinib (BTKi), Belumosudil (ROCK2i)
RefractoryRuxolitinib (REACH2/3), Ecp, Tofacitinib, MSC, Anti-CD47Ruxolitinib, Ibrutinib, Belumosudil, Ecp, Extracorporeal Photopheresis

Engraftment & Chimerism

MilestoneTimingSignificance
Neutrophil EngraftmentANC >0.5x10⁹/L (3 consecutive days)Day +14 to +21 (MAC), +21 to +28 (RIC)
Platelet EngraftmentPlt >20x10⁹/L (Unsupported 7d)Day +21 to +35
Full Donor Chimerism>95% DonorDay +30 to +100
Mixed ChimerismRecipient + DonorRIC/NMA, May be Stable (DLI if Relapse)
Chimerism MonitoringSTR/NGS (Peripheral Blood, BM)Monthly x3m, then q3m x1y, then q6m

6️⃣ Post-Transplant Monitoring

Kidney Transplant

ParameterFrequencyAction Threshold
Serum Creatinine / eGFRWeekly x1m, Biweekly x3m, Monthly x1y, q3m↑>20% from Baseline → Biopsy
Proteinuria (uPCR/uACR)Monthly x3m, q3m>0.5g/g → Biopsy
DSA (HLA Class I/II)Month 1, 3, 6, 12, then q6-12mNew DSA / Rising MFI → Biopsy ± PLEX/IVIG
dd-cfDNAMonth 1, 3, 6, 12, q6m>1% (Kidney), >0.5% (Heart) → Biopsy
Doppler US (Renal Arterial/ Venous Flow)Post-op Day 1, 1w, 1m, 3m, 6m, 1yResistive Index >0.8, Arterial Stenosis
BK Virus (Urine/Plasma PCR)Monthly x6m, q3m x2y>10⁴ copies/mL → Reduce IS, Leflunomide/Cidofovir
CMV/EBV PCRWeekly x3m, q2w x6mCMV >1000 IU/mL → Pre-emptive Valganciclovir

Heart/Lung Transplant Monitoring

ParameterFrequencyAction
Endomyocardial Biopsy (EMB)Weekly x4w, Biweekly x3m, Monthly x1y, q3mISHLT Grade ≥2R → Augment IS
DSA / dd-cfDNAq3-6mDSA+ / dd-cfDNA >0.5% → Biopsy
Spirometry (FEV1)Weekly x1m, Monthly x6m, q3mFEV1 Decline >10% → Biopsy, Augment IS
Bronchoscopy + BALSurveillance (3m, 12m)Infection, Rejection, Lymphocytic Bronchitis

Infection Prophylaxis (Post-Transplant)

PeriodKey Prophylaxis
0-1 MonthPJP (Co-trimoxazole), HSV/VZV (Acyclovir/Valaciclovir), Antibacterial (Co-trimoxazole covers PJP+UTI)
1-6 MonthsCMV (Valganciclovir Pre-emptive / Prophylaxis) — High Risk (D+/R-): 3-6m, BK Virus Monitoring, Fungal (Posaconazole/Voriconazole if High Risk), Adenovirus PCR monthly (Pediatric/HSCT), HHV-6 PCR (HSCT), Aspergillus (Posaconazole/Voriconazole if high risk)
6-12 MonthsCMV Prophylaxis Ends, BK Virus Monitoring, Annual Flu, Pneumococcal
>1 YearAnnual Flu, Pneumococcal (PCV20 → PPV23), Shingrix (If >50), COVID Boosters

⚡ FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
HLAClass I (A,B,C) = CD8; Class II (DR,DQ,DP) = CD4; Matching: Kidney (A,B,DR), HSCT (A,B,C,DRB1,DQB1 10/10)
AllorecognitionDirect (Donor HLA on Donor APC) = Early ACR; Indirect (Donor peptides on Recipient APC) = Chronic/AMR
RejectionHyperacute (Pre-formed DSA, CDC-XM+); ACR (Banff t/i, Pulse Steroids); AMR (DSA+, C4d+, g+ptc, PLEX/IVIG/Rituximab); Chronic (cg, cv, IF/TA)
ImmunosuppressionInduction: Basiliximab (Standard), ATG/Alemtuzumab (High Risk); Maintenance: Tac + MMF + Pred (Standard); Belatacept (CNI-Free, EBV+ only)
HSCTMAC vs RIC; MSD > MUD > Haplo (PTCy) > Cord; aGvHD <100d (Skin/GI/Liver), cGvHD >100d (Sclerotic/Sicca/BOS)
GvHD ProphylaxisMSD/MUD: Tac + MTX/MMF; Haplo: PTCy (Day +3, +4) + Tac + MMF (Standard)
GvHD TreatmentaGvHD: Steroids → Ruxolitinib/ATG; cGvHD: Steroids → Ruxolitinib → ECP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil
MonitoringKidney: Cr/eGFR, Proteinuria, DSA, dd-cfDNA, BK/CMV PCR; Heart: EMB (ISHLT), DSA, dd-cfDNA; HSCT: Chimerism, Immune Reconstitution
Infection ProphylaxisPJP (Co-trimoxazole), CMV (Valganciclovir D+/R-), HSV/VZV (Acyclovir), BKV (PCR Monitoring)
BelataceptEBV+ Only, CNI-Free, Monthly IV, ↑ PTLD Risk if EBV-

🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1Hyperacute vs Acute Cellular Rejection?Hyperacute: Pre-formed DSA, Complement activation, Minutes-Hours, Irreversible; ACR: T-cell mediated, Banff t/i, Days-Weeks, Reversible with Pulse Steroids
2Banff Classification — AMR criteria?DSA+, C4d+ (C4d2/3), Microvascular Inflammation (g>0 and/or ptc>0), Acute Tubular Injury
3ACR vs AMR — key difference?ACR: T-cell mediated (Biopsy: Tubulitis/Interstitial Inflammation), DSA-; AMR: Antibody-mediated (DSA+, C4d+, Microvascular inflammation)
4Tacrolimus vs Cyclosporine — key differences?Tac: More Potent, ↓ Nephrotoxicity, ↑ Neurotoxicity, ↑ Diabetes, ↓ Hyperlipidaemia; CSA: ↑ Gingival Hyperplasia, Hirsutism, Hypertension
5Belatacept — indication & contraindication?EBV+ Only, CNI-Sparing, Monthly IV, Contraindicated if EBV- (↑ PTLD Risk)
6GvHD Prophylaxis — Haploidentical HSCT?PTCy (Day +3, +4) + Tac + MMF — Standard of Care
7aGvHD vs cGvHD — timing & features?aGvHD <100d: Skin/GI/Liver; cGvHD >100d: Sclerotic, Sicca, BOS, Fasciitis, Ocular
7aGvHD Grade II — treatment?Prednisolone 1-2mg/kg; Refractory → Ruxolitinib/ATG
8cGvHD — 1st-line treatment?Prednisolone 0.5-1mg/kg + Tacrolimus/MMF; Refractory → Ruxolitinib/EKP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil
9HSCT Monitoring — chimerism?STR/NGS; Monthly x3m → q3m x1y → q6m; Target Full Donor (>95%)
10Post-Kidney Transplant Monitoring — dd-cfDNA threshold?>1% (Kidney) → Biopsy; Heart >0.5%; Serial monitoring for Rejection

🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"Hyperacute = ACR"NO. Hyperacute = Pre-formed DSA, Minutes-Hours, Irreversible; ACR = T-cell, Days-Weeks, Reversible
"C4d+ = AMR Always"NO. C4d can be negative in AMR (C4d-negative AMR); C4d+ without DSA = Not AMR (Accommodation)
"ACR = Only T-Cell"NO. ACR is T-cell mediated but AMR can coexist (Mixed Rejection)
"ACR = Steroid Resistant = AMR"NO. Steroid-Resistant ACR may need Ruxolitinib/ATG, Not automatically AMR
"Belatacept = For All Transplants"NO. EBV+ Only (PTLD Risk if EBV-), Kidney Only (Not Heart/Lung approved), Monthly IV
"PTCy = Only for Haplo"Also Used in MUD with ATG, Some Cord Blood Protocols, Mismatched Unrelated
"aGvHD = Only Skin"NO. Triad: Skin (Rash), GI (Diarrhoea), Liver (Bilirubin) — Lung (BOOP) in Late aGvHD
"cGvHD = Just Skin"NO. Multi-organ: Skin (Sclerotic), Eyes (Sicca), Mouth (Lichenoid), Lung (BOS), Liver, GI, Fascia, Genital
"Chronic Rejection = Only AMR"NO. Chronic Active TCMR (cv, IF/TA) + Chronic Active AMR (cg, ptcml) often Coexist
"dd-cfDNA = Replaces Biopsy"NO. Adjunct Only — Biopsy = Gold Standard; dd-cfDNA = Surveillance/Rule-Out
"Belatacept = CNI Replacement for All"NO. EBV+ Only, Not for Heart/Lung (Higher Rejection), Monthly IV Infusion
"PTCy = No GvHD"Reduces GvHD (Grade III-IV ↓) but Does Not Eliminate; cGvHD Still Occurs
"cGvHD = Just Fibrosis"NO. Multisystem: Skin (Sclerotic), Eyes (Sicca), Mouth (Lichenoid), Lung (BOS), GI, Liver, Fascia, Genital
"Belatacept = No Infection Risk"NO. ↑ PTLD (EBV-), ↑ CMV, ↑ BK Virus vs CNI (Different Profile)
"cGvHD = Treated with Steroids Only"NO. Ruxolitinib (1st-line Refractory), Ibrutinib, Belumosudil, ECP, Extracorporeal Photopheresis
Mnemonic: TRANSPLANT IMMUNOLOGY
Transplant Immunology: HLA (Class I A/B/C → CD8; Class II DR/DQ/DP → CD4)
Rejection: Hyperacute (DSA, CDC-XM+), ACR (Banff t/i, Pulse Steroid), AMR (DSA+, C4d+, g/ptc, PLEX/IVIG/Ritux)
Allorecognition: Direct (Donor APC), Indirect (Recipient APC), Semi-Direct
Nephrology Rejection: Banff t/i (ACR), cg/cv/ptc (Chronic), C4d/g/ptc (AMR)
Suppression: Induction (Basiliximab/ATG/Alemtuzumab) → Maintenance (Tac+MMF+Pred, Belatacept EBV+)
Pharmacology: Tac vs CSA (Tac More Potent, Neuro/DM; CSA: Hirsutism/Gingival/HTN)
LHLT: MAC vs RIC/NMA, MSD > MUD > Haplo (PTCy) > Cord, GvHD Prophylaxis (PTCy Haplo)
GvHD: aGvHD <100d (Skin/GI/Liver), cGvHD >100d (Sclerotic/Sicca/BOS)
GvHD Treatment: aGvHD (Steroids → Ruxolitinib), cGvHD (Steroids → Ruxolitinib/ECP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil)
Angiogenesis: Belatacept (CTLA4-Ig, EBV+, Monthly IV, CNI-Free, PTLD Risk)
New Monitoring: dd-cfDNA (>1% Kidney, >0.5% Heart), DSA, Gene Expression (AlloMap), Biopsy (Banff/ISHLT)
Tolerogenicity: Costim Blockade (CTLA4-Ig), Treg Therapy (Experimental), Mixed Chimerism

🗺️ Mind Map

Transplant Immunology
HLA
Class I: A, B, C → CD8
Class II: DR, DQ, DP → CD4
Matching: Kidney A,B,DR; HSCT 10/10
Epitope Matching: Eplet Mismatch Load
Allorecognition
Direct: Donor APC → Early ACR
Indirect: Recipient APC → Chronic/AMR
Semi-Direct: Exosomes/Trogocytosis
Rejection
Hyperacute: DSA, CDC-XM+, Minutes
ACR: Banff t/i, Pulse Steroid
AMR: DSA+, C4d+, g+ptc, PLEX/IVIG/Rituximab
Chronic: cg (Glomerulopathy), cv (Vascular), IF/TA
Immunosuppression
Induction: Basiliximab (Std), ATG/Alemtuzumab (High Risk)
Maintenance: Tac+MMF+Pred (Std), Belatacept (EBV+)
CNI: Tac (Potent, Neuro/DM), CSA (Hirsutism, Gum Hyperplasia)
mTOR: SRL/EVR (Lipids, Wound, Proteinuria)
Antimetabolite: MMF (GI, Leukopenia), AZA (TPMT)
Belatacept: CTLA4-Ig, EBV+, Monthly IV, CNI-Free
HSCT
Indications: AML/ALL, Thal/SCD, Aplastic, SID
Donor: MSD > MUD > Haplo (PTCy) > Cord
Conditioning: MAC (Bu/Cy, TBI/Cy) vs RIC (Flu/Mel)
GVHD: aGvHD <100d (Skin/GI/Liver), cGvHD >100d (Sclerotic/Sicca/BOS)
Prophylaxis: PTCy (Haplo), Tac+MTX/MMF (Std)
Treatment: aGvHD (Steroids→Ruxolitinib), cGvHD (Steroids→Ruxolitinib/ECP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil)
Engraftment: ANC>0.5, Plt>20, Chimerism >95% Donor
Chimerism: STR/qPCR, Monthly→q3m→q6m
Monitoring
Kidney: Cr/eGFR, Proteinuria, DSA, dd-cfDNA, BKV, CMV
Heart: EMB (ISHLT), DSA, dd-cfDNA, FEV1
Lung: Spirometry, BAL, Biopsy
HSCT: Chimerism (STR), Immune Reconstitution (CD4, CD8, B, NK)
Infections
PJP (Cotrimoxazole), CMV (Valganciclovir D+/R-), HSV/VZV (Acyclovir)
BKV (PCR Monitoring), Fungal (Posaconazole if High Risk)

💬 Exam Answer Modes

FormatPromptKey Points
Long Essay"Describe the mechanisms of allograft rejection and the principles of immunosuppression in kidney transplantation."HLA, Allorecognition (Direct/Indirect), Hyperacute/ACR/AMR Chronic, Banff Classification, Induction/Maintenance IS, CNI/mTOR/Antimetabolite/Belatacept, Monitoring
Short Note"Antibody-Mediated Rejection (AMR) — diagnosis and treatment."DSA+, C4d+, Microvascular Inflammation (g, ptc), PLEX/IVIG/Rituximab, Eculizumab (Refractory), Chronic AMR (cg, ptcml)
Viva"What is the difference between direct and indirect allorecognition?"Direct = Recipient T cells recognise Intact Donor HLA on Donor APCs (Early, Strong); Indirect = Recipient T cells recognise Processed Donor HLA Peptides on Recipient APCs (Chronic, AMR)
Ward Round"Renal transplant recipient Day +14, Creatinine rising, DSA Class II positive, C4d+. Next step?"AMR — Pulse Methylpred 500mg x3d + PLEX 5 exchanges + IVIG 2g/kg, Rituximab 375mg/m2, Optimise Maintenance (Tac Levels, MMF Dose), Consider Eculizumab if Refractory
Last-Night"HLA: Class I (A/B/C/CD8), Class II (DR/DQ/DP/CD4). Rejection: Hyperacute(DSA/CDC+), ACR(Banff t/i), AMR(DSA+/C4d+/g+ptc), Chronic(cg/cv/ptc). Allorecog: Direct=Early ACR, Indirect=Chronic/AMR. IS: Basilix/ATG→Tac+MMF+Pred; Belatacept(EBV+). HSCT: MAC/RIC, MSD>MUD>Haplo(PTCy)>Cord. aGvHD<100d(Skin/GI/Liver), cGvHD>100d(Sclerotic/Sicca/BOS). aGvHD Rx: Steroids→Ruxo. cGvHD Rx: Steroids→Ruxo/ECP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil. Monitoring: Cr, DSA, dd-cfDNA>1%, BKV, CMV. Belatacept: EBV+ Only."Compressed.

📌 Summary

  • HLA: Class I (A,B,C) → CD8; Class II (DR,DQ,DP) → CD4; Matching: Kidney A,B,DR; HSCT 10/10 (A,B,C,DRB1,DQB1)
  • Allorecognition: Direct = Intact Donor HLA on Donor APC → Early ACR; Indirect = Processed Donor Peptides on Recipient APC → Chronic Rejection/AMR
  • Rejection: Hyperacute (DSA, CDC-XM+, Minutes); ACR (Banff t/i, Pulse Steroids); AMR (DSA+, C4d+, g+ptc, PLEX/IVIG/Rituximab); Chronic (cg, cv, IF/TA)
  • Immunosuppression: Induction (Basiliximab Standard, ATG/Alemtuzumab High Risk); Maintenance: Tac + MMF + Pred (Standard), Belatacept (EBV+, CNI-Free, Monthly IV); mTOR (Sirolimus/Everolimus — Lipids, Wound, Proteinuria)
  • HSCT: Indications (AML, Thal, SCD, Aplastic, SID); Donor: MSD > MUD > Haplo (PTCy) > Cord; Conditioning: MAC (Bu/Cy) vs RIC (Flu/Mel); GvHD Prophylaxis: PTCy (Haplo), Tac+MTX/MMF (Standard)
  • GvHD: aGvHD <100d (Skin/GI/Liver, MAGIC Grading); cGvHD >100d (Sclerotic/Sicca/BOS, NIH Consensus); Treatment: Steroids → Ruxolitinib (1st-line Refractory) → ECP/Ibrutinib/Belumosudil/ECP
  • Monitoring: Kidney (Cr, DSA, dd-cfDNA>1%, BKV, CMV); Heart (EMB ISHLT, DSA, dd-cfDNA>0.5%); HSCT (Chimerism STR, Immune Reconstitution)
  • Infections: PJP (Cotrimoxazole), CMV (Valganciclovir D+/R-), HSV/VZV (Acyclovir), BKV (PCR, Reduce IS)
  • Belatacept: EBV+ Only, CNI-Free, Monthly IV, ↑ PTLD if EBV-

❓ MCQs (10)

  1. Hyperacute rejection mechanism?

A. T-cell mediated B. Pre-formed DSA + Complement Activation C. Cytokine Storm D. Macrophage Activation

Answer: B. Pre-formed DSA bind donor endothelium → Complement activation → Thrombosis/Necrosis within minutes-hours.

  1. Direct allorecognition involves:

A. Recipient T cells + Donor peptides on Recipient APC B. Recipient T cells + Intact Donor HLA on Donor APC C. Donor T cells + Recipient HLA D. Antibody-mediated

Answer: B. Direct = Recipient T cells recognise Intact Donor HLA on Donor APCs (Passenger Leukocytes).

  1. AMR diagnostic triad (Banff)?

A. DSA+, C4d+, Glomerulitis B. DSA+, C4d+, Microvascular Inflammation (g+ptc) C. DSA+, Tubulitis, Interstitial Inflammation D. C4d+, Tubulitis, Fibrosis

Answer: B. AMR = DSA+ + C4d+ (C4d2/3) + Microvascular Inflammation (g>0 and/or ptc>0).

  1. Belatacept — contraindication?

A. Diabetes B. EBV Seronegative C. Age >65 D. Prior Transplant

Answer: B. EBV Seronegative → High PTLD Risk. Belatacept only for EBV+ recipients.

  1. PTCy (Post-Transplant Cyclophosphamide) — indication?

A. All HSCT B. Haploidentical HSCT (Standard) C. Only MUD D. Only Cord Blood

Answer: B. PTCy Day +3 and +4 is Standard GVHD Prophylaxis for Haploidentical HSCT.

  1. Acute GvHD — classic triad?

A. Fever, Rash, Diarrhoea B. Skin (Rash), GI (Diarrhoea), Liver (Bilirubin) C. Fever, Cough, Rash D. Neuropathy, Rash, Diarrhoea

Answer: B. Classic Triad: Skin (Rash), GI (Diarrhoea/Nausea), Liver (Bilirubin ↑).

  1. Chronic GvHD — characteristic features?

A. Acute rash + Diarrhoea B. Sclerotic Skin, Sicca, Bronchiolitis Obliterans (BOS), Fasciitis, Ocular C. Acute Hepatitis + Rash D. Neutropenia + Fever

Answer: B. cGvHD = Sclerotic Skin, Sicca Syndrome, Bronchiolitis Obliterans (BOS), Fasciitis, Ocular Involvement.

  1. aGvHD Grade II — first-line treatment?

A. ATG B. Prednisolone 1-2mg/kg C. Ruxolitinib D. IVIG

Answer: B. Steroid (Pred 1-2mg/kg) first-line; Refractory → Ruxolitinib/ATG.

  1. Belatacept — mechanism of action?

A. Calcineurin Inhibitor B. CTLA-4-Ig (Blocks CD28-CD80/86 Costimulation) C. mTOR Inhibitor D. Antimetabolite

Answer: B. CTLA-4-Ig → Blocks CD28-CD80/86 Costimulation Signal 2 → T Cell Anergy.

  1. Chronic Antibody-Mediated Rejection — Banff features?

A. Tubulitis, Interstitial Inflammation B. Transplant Glomerulopathy (cg), Peritubular Capillary Basement Membrane Multilayering (ptcml), DSA+ C. C4d+ Only D. Endarteritis Only

Answer: B. Chronic AMR = cg (Transplant Glomerulopathy) + ptcml + DSA+.

  1. dd-cfDNA threshold for Kidney Transplant Rejection?

A. >0.5% B. >1% C. >2% D. >5%

Answer: B. >1% for Kidney Transplant (Heart >0.5%).

  1. Belatacept — mechanism?

A. Calcineurin Inhibitor B. CTLA-4-Ig (Blocks CD28-CD80/86) C. mTOR Inhibitor D. Antimetabolite

Answer: B. CTLA-4-Ig binds CD80/86 → Blocks CD28 Costimulation → T Cell Anergy.

📋 SBAs (10)

  1. Renal transplant recipient Day +30, Creatinine rising from 120 to 210. DSA Class II positive, C4d+ (C4d2). Biopsy: g2, ptc2, cg1. Diagnosis?

A. Acute Cellular Rejection B. Acute Antibody-Mediated Rejection C. Chronic AMR D. Acute Tubular Necrosis

Answer: B. DSA+ + C4d+ + Microvascular Inflammation (g2, ptc2) = Acute AMR.

  1. Haploidentical HSCT donor. GVHD Prophylaxis standard?

A. Tac + MMF B. PTCy (Day +3, +4) + Tac + MMF C. ATG + Tac + MMF D. Cyclophosphamide (Pre-transplant)

Answer: B. PTCy Day +3 and +4 + Tac + MMF = Standard for Haploidentical HSCT.

  1. Renal transplant recipient, Day +180. Creatinine stable. DSA Class I develops (MFI 3500). C4d negative. Biopsy: cg1, ptcml1. Diagnosis?

A. Acute AMR B. Chronic Active AMR C. Chronic TCMR D. No Rejection

Answer: B. Chronic Active AMR = DSA+ + cg>0 + ptcml>0 (C4d can be negative).

  1. HSCT Day +100. Patient with sclerodermatous skin changes, dry eyes, dry mouth, FEV1 60% predicted. Diagnosis?

A. Acute GvHD Grade III B. Chronic GvHD C. Infection C. Drug Reaction

Answer: B. >100 Days + Sclerotic Skin + Sicca + BOS (FEV1↓) = Chronic GvHD.

  1. Renal transplant recipient on Tacrolimus. Tremor, Headache, Hyperglycaemia. Trough Level 15 ng/mL. Action?

A. Increase Dose B. Reduce Dose (Target 5-10 ng/mL) C. Switch to Cyclosporine D. Add SIROLIMUS

Answer: B. Tacrolimus Trough 15 ng/mL = Supra-therapeutic → Neurotoxicity (Tremor, Headache) + Hyperglycaemia → Reduce Dose.

▸ 4.6.01 Tumour Immunology Immunotherapy

🎯 Learning Objectives

  • [ ] Explain Cancer Immunoediting — Elimination, Equilibrium, Escape
  • [ ] Classify Tumour Antigens — TSAs, TAAs, Neoantigens, Cancer-Testis Antigens
  • [ ] Apply Immune Checkpoint Inhibitors — PD-1/PD-L1, CTLA-4, LAG-3, TIGIT, TIM-3 — Indications, irAEs, Biomarkers

  • [ ] Apply Biomarkers — PD-L1, TMB, MSI, Neoantigen Load, IFN-γ Signature
  • [ ] Manage irAEs — Endocrine, GI, Hepatic, Pulmonary, Cardiac, Neurological
  • [ ] Answer viva: "PD-1 vs CTLA-4" and "CAR-T Toxicities (CRS/ICANS)" and "Biomarkers for ICI"

🧠 Core Concept: Cancer Immunoediting

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Cancer Immunoediting
↓
Elimination Immune Surveillance
↓
Equilibrium Dormancy / Editing
↓
Escape Immune Evasion
↓
Loss of Antigen Presentation MHC I Loss, B2M Mutations
Immunosuppressive Microenvironment Tregs, MDSCs, TAMs, CAFs, Cytokines (TGF-β, IL-10, VEGF)
Immune Checkpoint Upregulation PD-L1, CTLA-4, LAG-3, TIM-3, TIGIT, VISTA
Metabolic Dysregulation IDO, Arginase, Adenosine, Lactate, Hypoxia
Antigen Loss / Mutation Neoantigen Loss, Antigen Presentation Defects

1️⃣ Tumour Antigens

CategoryDefinitionExamplesClinical Relevance
TSAs (Tumour-Specific Antigens)Unique to tumour, Not in normal tissueNeoantigens (Non-synonymous mutations), Viral Antigens (HPV E6/E7, EBV LMP1/2)True Targets — No off-tumour toxicity; Neoantigen Vaccines, TCR-T
TAAs (Tumour-Associated Antigens)Expressed in tumours + Normal tissues (Overexpressed/Developmental)Differentiation (Tyrosinase, gp100, MART-1, NY-ESO-1), Overexpressed (HER2, EGFR, CEA, MUC1), Cancer-Testis (NY-ESO-1, MAGE-A)Cross-Reactivity Risk (On-target/off-tumour), Vaccines, CAR-T
NeoantigensMHC-presented peptides from somatic mutationsSNVs, Indels, Frameshifts, Fusions, Splicing VariantsPersonalised Vaccines, TCR-T, Predict ICI Response

Cancer-Testis Antigens (CTAs)

AntigenExpressionCancer Types
NY-ESO-1Testis, Melanoma, Sarcoma, Lung, Ovarian, BladderHigh Immunogenicity, Vaccines, TCR-T
MAGE-A Family (A1, A3, A4, A10)Germ cells, Melanoma, Lung, Oesophageal, BladderTCR-T, Vaccines
MAGE-C2Testis, Lung, Head & NeckImmunotherapy Target

2️⃣ Immune Checkpoint Inhibitors (ICIs)

Key Checkpoint Pathways

CheckpointLigandExpressionMechanismClinical Effect
PD-1PD-L1 (B7-H1), PD-L2T cells, B cells, NK, Macrophages (Activated)Inhibits TCR/CD28 signalling → SHP-2 recruitment → ↓ PI3K/Akt, ↓ TCR signallingExhaustion, Apoptosis, Anergy
CTLA-4CD80 (B7-1), CD86 (B7-2)T cells (Activated), Tregs (Constitutive)Competes with CD28 for B7 binding → No Co-stimulation, Trans-endocytosis of CD80/86Early Activation Block, Treg Function
LAG-3 (CD223)MHC Class II, FGL1, LSECtinActivated T/NK cells, TregsInhibits TCR signalling, Enhances Treg suppressionExhaustion, Synergy with PD-1
TIGITCD155 (PVR), CD112, CD113T/NK cells, TregsCompetes with CD226 (DNAM-1) → ↓ Adhesion/Cytotoxicity, ↑ TregExhaustion, Synergy with PD-1
TIM-3Galectin-9, CEACAM1, HMGB1, PSExhausted T/NK, Tregs, DCsInhibits TCR signalling, ↓ CytokinesTerminal Exhaustion
VISTAVSIG3, PSGL-1Myeloid, T cells (Naive)Inhibits T cell activation, Acidic pHMyeloid Suppression
B7-H3 (CD276)UnknownTumour, Myeloid, T cellsCo-stimulatory/InhibitoryTumour Immune Evasion
B7-H4UnknownTumour, MacrophagesInhibits T cell proliferationTumour Immune Evasion

HCCPD-L1, AFP, TMBAtezo+Bev, Durvalumab+Treme, Pembro+Lenvatinib
UrothelialPD-L1, TMB, FGFR3Pembro, Atezo, Nivo, Avelumab
HNSCCPD-L1 (CPS), HPV, TMBPembro 1L (CPS≥1), Nivo 2L
TNBCPD-L1, TMB, BRCA, TILsPembro (PD-L1 CPS≥10), Atezo+Nab-Paclitaxel
MSI-H/dMMR (Any Solid Tumour)MSI-H/dMMRPembrolizumab (Tumour-Agnostic)
TMB-H (≥10 mut/Mb)TMB-HPembrolizumab (Tumour-Agnostic)

4️⃣ Adoptive Cell Therapies

CAR-T Cells

ComponentDetail
StructurescFv (Antigen Binding) + Hinge + Transmembrane + Costimulatory (CD28/4-1BB) + CD3ζ (Signalling)
Generations1st: CD3ζ only; 2nd: +CD28/4-1BB; 3rd: +CD28+4-1BB; 4th: +Cytokine (IL-12, IL-15) "Armoured"; 5th: +JAK/STAT
Approved ProductsCD19: Tisagenlecleucel (Kymriah), Axicabtagene Ciloleucel (Yescarta), Lisocabtagene Maraleucel (Breyanzi), Idecabtagene Vicleucel (Abecma); BCMA: Idecabtagene Vicleucel (Abecma), Ciltacabtagene Autoleucel (Carvykti)
IndicationsCD19: R/R B-ALL (≤25y), R/R DLBCL (2L+), R/R FL (3L+); BCMA: R/R Multiple Myeloma (4L+)

CAR-T Toxicities — CRS & ICANS

ToxicityGrading (ASTCT 2019)Management
CRS (Cytokine Release Syndrome)Grade 1: Fever; Grade 2: Hypotension (1 Vasopressor) / Hypoxia (Low-flow O₂); Grade 3: Hypotension (≥2 Vasopressors) / Hypoxia (High-flow O₂); Grade 4: Life-threatening (Ventilator, ≥3 Vasopressors)Tocilizumab 8mg/kg (Max 800mg) IV — 1st Line; Siltuximab (Alternative); Steroids (Dex 10mg q6h) if Refractory/Grade ≥3; Supportive Care
ICANS (Immune Effector Cell-Associated Neurotoxicity Syndrome)Grade 1: Awake, ICE Score 7-9; Grade 2: Awake, ICE 3-6; Grade 3: Obtunded (ICE 0-2); Grade 4: Coma (ICE 0), Seizure, Cerebral OedemaDexamethasone 10mg IV q6h (Grade ≥2); Tocilizumab if CRS co-existent; Anti-Seizure, ICU, Avoid Tocilizumab Monotherapy for ICANS (BBB penetration poor)
CRS/ICANS MonitoringFrequency
First 14-28 Daysq8-12h (Vitals, Neuro Exam ICE Score, Labs)
CRS Grade ≥2q2-4h; ICANS Grade ≥2 q1-2h

5️⃣ Immunotherapy Toxicities (irAEs) — Immune-Related Adverse Events

irAE Grading (CTCAE v5.0)

GradeDefinition
Grade 1Mild; Asymptomatic or Mild symptoms; Clinical/diagnostic observations only
Grade 2Moderate; Minimal, Local, Non-invasive intervention indicated
Grade 3Severe; Medically significant; Hospitalisation indicated
Grade 4Life-threatening; Urgent intervention indicated
Grade 5Death

irAE Incidence & Timing

irAEMedian OnsetIncidence (Anti-PD-1)Incidence (Combo Ipi+Nivo)
Thyroiditis6-12 weeks5-10%10-15%
Colitis6-14 weeks10-15% (Grade 3-4: 1-2%)25-30% (Grade 3-4: 10-15%)
Hepatitis6-12 weeks5-10% (Grade 3-4: 2-5%)15-25% (Grade 3-4: 5-10%)
Pneumonitis2-6 months3-5% (Grade 3-4: 1-3%)5-10% (Grade 3-4: 2-5%)
Hypophysitis8-12 weeks2-5% (Anti-CTLA-4 > PD-1)5-10% (Combo)
Adrenal Insufficiency8-16 weeks1-3%5-8%
Dermatitis3-6 weeks20-30% (Grade 3-4: 1-2%)40-50% (Grade 3-4: 5-10%)
Neurological (Guillain-Barré, Myasthenia, Encephalitis)Variable<1-2%2-5%
Cardiac (Myocarditis, Pericarditis)2-12 weeks<1% (Grade 3-4: <1%)1-2% (Grade 3-4: 1-2%)
Renal (Nephritis)8-14 weeks1-2%2-5%
Ocular (Uveitis, Dry Eye)6-12 weeks1-2%2-5%
Musculoskeletal (Arthralgia, Myositis)6-12 weeks10-20%20-30%

irAE Management Principles

GradeICI ManagementSteroidAdditional
Grade 1Continue ICITopical (Dermatitis) / NoneSymptomatic
Grade 2Hold ICIPrednisolone 0.5-1mg/kgTopical, Loperamide (Colitis), Antacids (Hepatitis)
Grade 3Hold ICIIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kgInfliximab 5mg/kg (Colitis Refractory), MMF/Tacrolimus (Hepatitis Refractory)
Grade 4Permanently DiscontinueIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kgICU, Infliximab (Colitis), MMF/Tac (Hepatitis), IVIG (Myocarditis/Neurological)

Organ-Specific irAE Management

irAEGrade 1-2Grade 3-4
ColitisLoperamide, Budesonide, Pred 0.5-1mg/kgIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, Infliximab 5mg/kg (Refractory), Vedolizumab, Tofacitinib
HepatitisLFT Monitoring, Pred 0.5-1mg/kgIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, MMF 1g BD, Tacrolimus, IVIG
PneumonitisPred 0.5-1mg/kg, Hold ICIIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, Infliximab, Cyclophosphamide, IVIG
Endocrine (Thyroiditis, Hypophysitis, Adrenal, T1DM)Hormone Replacement (Levothyroxine, Hydrocortisone, Insulin)Hormone Replacement + High-Dose Steroids (Pituitary)
DermatitisTopical Steroids, Oral Pred 0.5mg/kgIV Methylpred, IVIG, Cyclosporine
PneumonitisHold ICI, Pred 1mg/kgIV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, Infliximab, Cyclophosphamide
Key: Endocrinopathies = Hormone Replacement + Steroids (Usually Permanent), Colitis/Hepatitis/Pneumonitis = Steroids + Immunosuppression if Refractory

6️⃣ Resistance Mechanisms & Combination Strategies

Primary Resistance

MechanismExample
Lack of Tumour AntigensLow TMB, No Neoantigens, MHC I Loss
Immune Exclusion"Cold Tumour" — Excluded T cells (Stroma, VEGF, CXCL12)
Immunosuppressive TMETregs, MDSCs, TAMs (M2), CAFs, TGF-β, IL-10, VEGF, IDO, Adenosine

Acquired Resistance

MechanismExample
Antigen LossMHC I Loss (B2M Mutation), Neoantigen Loss, Antigen Presentation Defects
Checkpoint UpregulationLAG-3, TIM-3, TIGIT, VISTA Upregulation
Signalling BypassJAK1/2 Mutations (IFN-γ Resistance), PTEN Loss (PI3K Activation)
Lineage PlasticityEMT, Neuroendocrine Transdifferentiation
Metabolic AdaptationIDO, Arg1, Adenosine, Lactate, Hypoxia

Combination Strategies to Overcome Resistance

StrategyCombinationRationale
Dual CheckpointPD-1 + CTLA-4 (Nivo+Ipi), PD-1 + LAG-3 (Nivo+Rela)Non-redundant pathways, Deeper T cell activation
ICI + ChemotherapyPembro + Chemo (NSCLC, TNBC, Gastric)Immunogenic Cell Death, Antigen Release, Lymphodepletion
ICI + Anti-AngiogenicPembro + Lenvatinib (Endometrial, RCC, HCC)Vascular Normalisation, ↓ MDSCs/Tregs, ↑ T Cell Infiltration
ICI + RadiotherapyPembro + RTAbscopal Effect, Antigen Release, STING Activation
ICI + Targeted TherapyPembro + Lenvatinib (RCC, Endometrial), Atezo + Bev (HCC)↓ VEGF → Vascular Normalisation + Immune Activation
ICI + EP4 AntagonistPembro + Grapafant (EP4 Antag)PGE2-EP4 → MDSC/Treg Suppression
ICI + STING AgonistPembro + STING AgonistInnate Immune Activation, DC Maturation
ICI + Oncolytic VirusT-VEC + PembroLocal Lysis → Antigen Release, Systemic Immune Activation

🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1Cancer immunoediting — three phases?Elimination (Immune Surveillance), Equilibrium (Dormancy/Editing), Escape (MHC Loss, Checkpoint Upregulation, TME Suppression)
2PD-1 vs CTLA-4 — mechanism difference?PD-1: Inhibits Effector Phase (Peripheral Tissues), PD-L1/PD-L2; CTLA-4: Inhibits Priming Phase (Lymph Node), Competes with CD28 for B7
3Anti-PD-1 vs Anti-CTLA-4 — toxicity difference?Anti-PD-1: Lower Grade 3-4 (10-15%), More Pneumonitis, Thyroiditis; Anti-CTLA-4: Higher Grade 3-4 (20-30%), More Colitis, Hypophysitis, Dermatitis
4PD-1 + CTLA-4 combination — rationale?Non-redundant Pathways: CTLA-4 (Priming/Lymph Node) + PD-1 (Effector/Peripheral) → Deeper, Broader T Cell Activation
5CAR-T CRS — grading & management?ASTCT 2019: Grade 1 (Fever), 2 (Hypotension 1 Vasopressor/Hypoxia Low-flow), 3 (Hypotension ≥2 Vasopressors/Hypoxia High-flow), 4 (Life-threatening); Tocilizumab 8mg/kg IV 1st Line; Steroids if Refractory
6CAR-T ICANS — management?Dex 10mg IV q6h (Grade ≥2); Tocilizumab if CRS Co-existent; Avoid Tocilizumab Monotherapy for ICANS (Poor BBB Penetration); ICU, Anti-seizure, Avoid Sedation
7. Key biomarkers for ICI response?PD-L1 (TPS/CPS/IC), MSI-H/dMMR (Pan-cancer), TMB-H (≥10 mut/Mb), Neoantigen Load, IFN-γ Signature
8. MSI-H vs TMB-H — difference?MSI-H = MMR Deficiency (IHC/MSI-PCR); TMB-H = High Mutational Burden (≥10 mut/Mb); Overlap but Distinct — POLE/POLD1 = TMB-H but MSS
9. CAR-T CRS Grade 3 management?Tocilizumab 8mg/kg IV (Max 800mg) + Dexamethasone 10mg IV q6h; ICU Monitoring; Avoid Tocilizumab for ICANS Alone
10. Anti-PD-1 + Anti-CTLA-4 — approval?Nivolumab + Ipilimumab — Melanoma, RCC, NSCLC (PD-L1≥1%), MPM, HCC, Urothelial, ESCC

🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"PD-1 and CTLA-4 do the same thing"NO. PD-1 = Peripheral/Effector Phase (Tissue); CTLA-4 = Priming Phase (Lymph Node). Non-redundant.
"All MSI-H = TMB-H"NO. Overlap but Distinct. POLE/POLD1 mutants = TMB-H but MSS (Not MSI-H).
"TMB-H = Always Respond to ICI"NO. Predictive but Not Perfect — Some TMB-H Tumours Resistant (Immune Exclusion, MHC Loss).
"CAR-T = Only for Leukaemia"NO. CD19 = B-ALL, DLBCL, FL; BCMA = Myeloma; GPC3, HER2, EGFRvIII in Solid Tumours (Trials).
"CRS = ICANS"NO. CRS = Cytokine Storm (Fever, Hypotension, Hypoxia); ICANS = Neurotoxicity (Encephalopathy, Seizures, Aphasia). Different Mechanisms/Treatments.
"Tocilizumab for ICANS"POOR CNS Penetration — Not 1st Line for ICANS Alone. Dexamethasone 1st Line for ICANS; Tocilizumab only if CRS Co-exists.
"MSI-H = Lynch Only"NO. Lynch = Germline MMR; MSI-H = Sporadic (MLH1 Methylation) + Lynch; Also in Gastric, Endometrial, CRC, Other.
"TMB-H = Only for ICI"NO. Also Predicts Chemo Response (High TMB → Better Chemo Response in Some Cancers).
"All irAEs = Stop ICI"NO. Grade 1-2 = Continue/Continue with Steroids; Grade 3-4 = Hold/Discontinue.
"Tocilizumab for All ICANS"NO. Poor CNS Penetration. Dexamethasone 1st Line for ICANS; Tocilizumab only if Concurrent CRS.
Mnemonic: TUMOUR IMMUNOLOGY IMMUNOTHERAPY
Tumour Immunoediting: Elimination → Equilibrium → Escape (MHC Loss, Checkpoints, TME)
Unique Antigens: TSAs (Neoantigens) vs TAAs (Differentiation/Overexpressed/Cancer-Testis)
Major Checkpoints: PD-1 (PD-L1/PD-L2), CTLA-4 (CD80/86), LAG-3 (MHC II), TIGIT (CD155), TIM-3 (Gal-9), VISTA
Oncolytic Viruses: T-VEC (HSV-1+GM-CSF) — Approved Melanoma
U (CAR-T): CD19 (B-ALL/DLBCL/FL), BCMA (Myeloma) — CRS/ICANS → Tocilizumab/Dex
Resistance: Primary (Cold Tumour, No Antigen), Acquired (MHC Loss, Checkpoint Up, JAK Mut, Lineage Switch)
ICIs: PD-1/PD-L1 (Pembro/Nivo/Atezo/Durva/Avel/Cemi), CTLA-4 (Ipi/Treme), LAG-3 (Relatlimab)
Immunotherapy Toxicity: irAEs — Colitis, Hepatitis, Pneumonitis, Hypophysitis, Thyroiditis, Dermatitis, Myocarditis
IrAE Management: Grade 1-2 Continue/Hold+Steroids; Grade 3-4 Hold/Stop+IV Steroids+Infliximab/IVIG
Biomarkers: PD-L1 (TPS/CPS/IC), MSI-H/dMMR, TMB-H (≥10), Neoantigen Load, IFN-γ Signature
Tumour-Agnostic: Pembrolizumab (MSI-H/dMMR, TMB-H)
Oncolytic Virus: T-VEC (HSV-1+GM-CSF) — Approved Melanoma
Resistance: Primary (Cold Tumour), Acquired (MHC Loss, Alt Checkpoints, JAK Mut, Lineage Switch)
Adoptive Therapy: CAR-T (CD19, BCMA), TCR-T (NY-ESO-1, MAGE-A4), TIL, NK, BiTE (Blina, Tecla)
Phase: 1st Gen (CD3ζ), 2nd (CD28/4-1BB), 3rd (CD28+4-1BB), 4th (Cytokine/Armoured), 5th (JAK/STAT)
Y (Why Resistance?): MHC Loss, Alt Checkpoints (LAG-3, TIM-3, TIGIT), JAK1/2 Mut, PTEN Loss, MET Amp, EMT
