📌 Summary

  • Cancer Immunoediting: Elimination → Equilibrium → Escape (MHC Loss, Checkpoint Upregulation, TME Suppression)
  • Antigens: TSAs (Neoantigens) = Unique; TAAs = Differentiation/Overexpressed/Cancer-Testis (Shared)
  • Checkpoint Inhibitors: PD-1/PD-L1 (Pembro, Nivo, Atezo, Durva, Avel, Cemi); CTLA-4 (Ipi, Treme); LAG-3 (Relatlimab); TIGIT/TIM-3/VISTA (Investigational)
  • Combo Regimens: Nivo+Ipi (Mel, RCC, NSCLC); Pembro+Lenvatinib (Endometrial, RCC, HCC); Atezo+Bev (HCC); Nivo+Rela (Melanoma)
  • Biomarkers: PD-L1 (TPS/CPS/IC), MSI-H/dMMR (Pan-cancer), TMB-H (≥10 mut/Mb), Neoantigen Load, IFN-γ Signature
  • CAR-T: CD19 (B-ALL, DLBCL, FL), BCMA (Myeloma); CRS/ICANS — Tocilizumab + Dex; ICANS → Dex 1st Line
  • irAEs: Colitis, Hepatitis, Pneumonitis, Hypophysitis, Thyroiditis, Dermatitis, Myocarditis — Steroids → Infliximab (Colitis), MMF/Tac (Hepatitis), IVIG (Myocarditis/Neuro)
  • Resistance: Primary (Cold Tumour) + Acquired (MHC Loss, Alt Checkpoints, JAK Mut, Lineage Switch)
  • Combination Strategies: ICI+Chemo, ICI+Anti-VEGF, ICI+RT, ICI+Targeted, ICI+Oncolytic, Dual Checkpoint
  • Tumour-Agnostic Approvals: Pembrolizumab (MSI-H/dMMR, TMB-H); Dostarlimab (MSI-H/dMMR); Nivolumab (MSI-H/dMMR)

❓ MCQs (10)

  1. Cancer immunoediting — phase where tumour is controlled but not eliminated?

A. Elimination B. Equilibrium C. Escape D. Progression

Answer: B. Equilibrium — Dormancy, Immune Editing, Tumour Dormancy.

  1. PD-1 vs CTLA-4 — key mechanistic difference?

A. PD-1 = Priming, CTLA-4 = Effector B. PD-1 = Effector (Peripheral), CTLA-4 = Priming (Lymph Node) C. Same Mechanism D. PD-1 = Treg, CTLA-4 = Teff

Answer: B. PD-1 = Inhibits Effector Phase (Peripheral Tissues); CTLA-4 = Inhibits Priming Phase (Lymph Node).

  1. Most specific biomarker for ICI response across cancers?

A. PD-L1 TPS B. MSI-H/dMMR (Pan-cancer) C. TMB D. IFN-γ Signature

Answer: B. MSI-H/dMMR = Tumour-Agnostic Approval (Pembrolizumab, Dostarlimab).

  1. CAR-T CRS Grade 3 management?

A. Steroids only B. Tocilizumab 8mg/kg IV + Dexamethasone C. Antibiotics D. IVIG

Answer: B. Tocilizumab 8mg/kg IV + Dexamethasone 10mg IV q6h.

  1. ICANS — first-line treatment?

A. Tocilizumab B. Dexamethasone 10mg IV q6h C. Anti-IL-6 D. Plasma Exchange

Answer: B. Dexamethasone 1st Line; Tocilizumab only if Concurrent CRS.

  1. MSI-H vs TMB-H — difference?

A. Same B. MSI = MMR Deficiency; TMB = Mutational Burden; Overlap but Distinct C. TMB-H subset of MSI-H D. MSI-H subset of TMB-H

Answer: B. MSI = MMR Deficiency; TMB = Mutational Burden; Overlap but Distinct (POLE = TMB-H, MSS).

  1. Anti-PD-1 + Anti-CTLA-4 — approved for?

A. Breast Cancer B. Melanoma, RCC, NSCLC (PD-L1≥1%), MPM, HCC, Urothelial C. All Solid Tumours D. Haematological Only

Answer: B. Nivo+Ipi approved for Melanoma, RCC, NSCLC (PD-L1≥1%), MPM, HCC, Urothelial.

  1. CAR-T CRS Grade 1 — clinical feature?

A. Hypotension B. Fever Only C. Hypoxia D. Organ Dysfunction

Answer: B. Grade 1 = Fever Only.

  1. Tumour-agnostic pembrolizumab approval based on:

A. PD-L1 TPS ≥50% B. MSI-H/dMMR OR TMB-H (≥10 mut/Mb) C. HER2+ D. ALK+

Answer: B. MSI-H/dMMR (Pan-cancer) + TMB-H ≥10 mut/Mb.

  1. ICANS Grade 2 — ICE Score?

A. 7-9 B. 3-6 C. 0-2 D. 10

Answer: B. ICE Score 3-6 = Grade 2 (Awake, Impaired).

📋 SBAs (10)

  1. Patient on pembrolizumab develops Grade 3 diarrhoea (8 stools/day), Cr 180. Management?

A. Continue pembrolizumab + Loperamide B. Hold pembrolizumab, IV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, Infliximab if Refractory C. Stop pembrolizumab permanently D. Add Budesonide

Answer: B. Grade 3 Colitis → Hold ICI, IV Methylpred 1-2mg/kg, Infliximab if Refractory.

  1. NSCLC, PD-L1 TPS 60%, no driver mutation. 1st line?

A. Chemotherapy B. Pembrolizumab Monotherapy C. Pembrolizumab + Chemo D. Nivolumab + Ipilimumab

Answer: B. PD-L1 TPS ≥50% → Pembrolizumab Monotherapy 1L (KEYNOTE-024).

  1. Melanoma, BRAF WT, Bulky Disease. Combination ICI?

A. Nivolumab Monotherapy B. Nivolumab + Ipilimumab C. Pembrolizumab + Lenvatinib D. Talimogene Laherparepvec

Answer: B. Nivo+Ipi Superior to Nivo Mono in High-Burden (CheckMate 067).

  1. CAR-T patient Day +5, Fever 39.5°C, Hypotension (MAP 55 on Norad 0.1), Hypoxia (O2 88% on 4L). CRS Grade?

A. Grade 1 B. Grade 3 (Hypotension ≥2 Vasopressors / High-Flow O2) C. Grade 2 D. Grade 4

Answer: B. Grade 3 = Hypotension Requiring ≥2 Vasopressors OR High-Flow O2.

  1. MSI-H endometrial cancer. Immunotherapy?

A. Chemotherapy B. Pembrolizumab (Tumour-Agnostic) C. Hormonal Therapy D. Radiotherapy

Answer: B. MSI-H/dMMR = Tumour-Agnostic Pembrolizumab Approval.

▸ 4.7.01 Immune Based Therapies

  • [ ] Apply Cytokine Therapies — G-CSF, GM-CSF, EPO, TPO, IFN-α/β/γ

🧠 Core Concept: Immune-Based Therapies

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Immune-Based Therapies
↓
Immunoglobulin Therapy IVIG / SCIG
Monoclonal Antibodies (mAbs)
Cytokine Therapies G-CSF, GM-CSF, EPO, TPO, IFN-α/β/γ
Small Molecule Immunomodulators S1P Modulators, BTK Inhibitors, BCL-2 Inhibitors
Cellular Therapies Treg, MSC, CAR-T, TCR-T
↓
Anti-TNF Infliximab, Adalimumab, Certolizumab, Golimumab, Etanercept
Anti-IL-6R Tocilizumab, Sarilumab
Anti-IL-17/23 Secukinumab, Ixekizumab, Ustekinumab, Risankizumab
Anti-IL-1 Anakinra, Canakinumab
Anti-CD20 Rituximab, Ofatumumab, Obinutuzumab
Anti-IL-4/13 Dupilumab
Anti-Integrin Vedolizumab, Natalizumab
Anti-CD38/BCMA Daratumumab, Teclistamab
JAK Inhibitors Tofacitinib, Baricitinib, Upadacitinib, Filgotinib

1️⃣ Immunoglobulin Therapy (IVIG / SCIG)

Mechanisms of Action

MechanismDescription
FcRn BlockadeSaturates FcRn → ↑ Catabolism of Endogenous IgG (Including Autoantibodies)
FcγRIIb EngagementInhibits B-Cell Activation, ↓ Autoantibody Production
Complement ScavengingBinds C3b/C4b → Prevents MAC Formation
Idiotypic NetworkAnti-Idiotypic Antibodies Neutralise Pathogenic Autoantibodies
Treg Expansion↑ Treg Function, ↑ IL-10/TGF-β
Cytokine Modulation↓ Pro-inflammatory (TNF, IL-1, IL-6, IL-17), ↑ IL-10, IL-1Ra
FcγR BlockadeBlocks FcγR on Macrophages/Neutrophils → ↓ Phagocytosis, ADCC
Complement InhibitionPrevents C5a/C5b-9 Formation

Indications (UK / International Guidelines)

CategoryIndicationsDose & Route
Primary ImmunodeficienciesXLA, CVID, Hyper-IgM, IgG Subclass Deficiency, Specific Antibody DeficiencyIVIG 400-600 mg/kg q3-4w OR SCIG 100-200 mg/kg/wk
NeurologicalCIDP (1st line), MMN, GBS (1st Line with PLEX), Myasthenia Gravis Crisis, LEMS, Autoimmune Encephalitis (Anti-NMDA, LGI1, CASPR2)IVIG 2g/kg over 2-5d (Course), SCIG Maintenance
HaematologicalITP (1st Line + Steroids), AIHA (Refractory), NAIT, HLA AlloimmunisationIVIG 1g/kg/d x2d (ITP), 2g/kg/d x2-5d (GBS)
AutoimmuneKawasaki Disease (Acute), Dermatomyositis, SLE (Refractory), ANCA Vasculitis (Refractory), Pemphigus/Pemphigoid, SJS/TENIVIG 2g/kg (Kawasaki + Aspirin), 1-2g/kg (Autoimmune)
TransplantABOi/HLAi Desensitisation, AMR Treatment, Post-Transplant Lymphoproliferative DisorderIVIG 1-2g/kg ± PLEX/RTX
InfectiousToxic Shock, Staphylococcal Scalded Skin, Enteroviral Meningitis, Parvovirus B19 (Pure Red Cell Aplasia)IVIG 1-2g/kg

IVIG vs SCIG

FeatureIVIGSCIG
RouteIntravenousSubcutaneous
FrequencyEvery 3-4 weeksWeekly (or 2x/week)
Peak IgGHigh (Rapid)Steady State (Lower Peak)
Adverse EffectsHeadache, Aseptic Meningitis, Thrombosis, AKI, HaemolysisLocal Site Reactions, Less Systemic
ConvenienceHospital/Outpatient InfusionHome Self-Administration
IgG Trough LevelsFluctuating (Peak 2-3d, Trough Day 21)Stable (Steady State)
CostHigher (Infusion Suite)Lower (Home)

Adverse Effects & Monitoring

Adverse EffectIncidencePrevention/Management
Headache / Aseptic Meningitis10-15%Slow Infusion Rate, Pre-hydration, Paracetamol/NSAID
Thrombosis (Arterial/Venous)<1%Hydration, Avoid in High Risk (Immobility, Malignancy, History VTE)
Acute Kidney Injury1-5% (Sucrose-containing)Avoid Sucrose Preparations, Hydration, Monitor Creatinine
Haemolysis<1% (ABO Mismatch)Avoid High Doses in Non-O Blood Groups
AnaphylaxisRare (IgA-Deficient + Anti-IgA)IgA-Deficient → IgA-Depleted IVIG
Transfusion-Related Acute Lung Injury (TRALI)RareMonitor Respiratory Status

Monitoring on IVIG/SCIG

ParameterFrequency
Pre-InfusionIgG Level, Renal Function, FBC, IgA (Screen Deficiency)
During InfusionVital Signs q15-30min, Infusion Rate Monitoring
Post-Infusion (IVIG)IgG Trough (Pre-Next Dose), Renal Function (If Risk)
Long-Term (SCIG)IgG Trough q3-6m, Local Site Assessment, Patient-Reported Outcomes

2️⃣ Monoclonal Antibodies (Therapeutic)

Anti-TNF Agents

DrugTypeIndicationsMonitoring
InfliximabChimeric Mouse-Human IgG1RA, AS, PsA, Crohn's, UC, Uveitis, Behçet's, SarcoidosisTB Screen (IGRA/TST) Pre-Tx, LFT, CBC q3-6m, LFT q3m
AdalimumabFully Human IgG1RA, PsA, AS, Crohn's, UC, Psoriasis, Hidradenitis, UveitisTB Screen, LFT, CBC q3-6m
Certolizumab PegolPEGylated Fab' Fragment (No Fc)Pregnancy Safe (No Placental Transfer), RA, PsA, AS, Crohn'sTB Screen, LFT, CBC q3-6m
GolimumabHuman IgG1RA, PsA, AS, UCTB Screen, LFT, CBC q3-6m
EtanerceptFusion Protein (TNFR2-Fc)RA, PsA, AS, JIA, PsoriasisTB Screen, LFT, CBC q3-6m

Key Adverse Effects (Anti-TNF)

Adverse EffectIncidenceManagement
TB Reactivation1-5% (Highest with Infliximab/Adalimumab)Mandatory LTBI Screen (IGRA/TST) Pre-Tx; Treat LTBI Before Start
Serious Infections3-5%Hold if Serious Infection; Prophylactic Antibiotics in High Risk
Malignancy (Lymphoma, Skin Cancer)Slight ↑Age-Appropriate Cancer Screening; Sun Protection
Demyelination (MS-like)RareDiscontinue if Confirmed
Heart Failure (Worsening/De Novo)RareAvoid in NYHA III/IV HF
Drug-Induced LupusRareDiscontinue, Usually Resolves

Anti-IL-6R (Tocilizumab, Sarilumab)

FeatureTocilizumabSarilumab
TargetIL-6R (Membrane + Soluble)IL-6R (Membrane + Soluble)
IndicationsRA (Inadequate MTX), GCA (1st Line + GC), sJIA, AOSD, Cytokine Release Syndrome (CRS), COVID-19 (Severe)RA (Inadequate MTX), GCA
DosingIV 8mg/kg q4w (RA), 162mg SC q2w (RA/GCA)200mg SC q2w
Key MonitoringLFT (ALT/AST ↑), Lipids (↑ TG/TC), Neutrophils, PlateletsSame
Key Adverse EffectsGI Perforation (Diverticulitis), Neutropenia, Hyperlipidaemia, Infections, HepatotoxicitySame

Anti-IL-17/IL-23 Pathway

DrugTargetIndicationsDosing
SecukinumabIL-17APsA, AS, Psoriasis (Mod-Sev), nr-axSpA300mg SC q4w (Load 300mg w0,1,2,3,4)
IxekizumabIL-17APsA, AS, Psoriasis160mg SC Load → 80mg q4w
BrodalumabIL-17RAPsoriasis210mg SC q2w (Load w0,1,2)

Guselkumab / Risankizumab / MirikizumabIL-23p19Psoriasis, PsA (Gus/Risa), CD/UC (Miri/Risa)q8w (Gus), q12w (Risa/Miri)
Key Difference: IL-23i (Ustekinumab/Guselkumab/Risankizumab) effective in PsA, NOT in AS/axSpA; IL-17i effective in AS/axSpA/PsA

JAK Inhibitors (Tofacitinib, Baricitinib, Upadacitinib, Filgotinib)

DrugSelectivityIndicationsKey Monitoring
TofacitinibJAK1/3RA, PsA, UC, ADCBC, LFT, Lipids, CK, VZV IgG, TB Screen, CVD Risk
BaricitinibJAK1/2RA, AD, COVID-19 (Hospitalised)Similar + CK, Lymphocytes
UpadacitinibJAK1RA, PsA, AD, UC, Crohn'sSimilar + CPK
FilgotinibJAK1RA, UCSimilar
Key Adverse Effects (Class Effect): Herpes Zoster (↑↑), VTE (PE/DVT), MACE (CV Events), Lipids ↑, Cytopenias, Liver Toxicity, Creatinine ↑
Contraindicated: Active TB, Active Serious Infection, Severe Hepatic Impairment, Pregnancy, Lymphocytes <500/μL, Hgb <8g/dL, ANC <1000/μL

🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1IVIG mechanisms of action?FcRn Blockade (↑ Catabolism of Autoantibodies), FcγRIIb Engagement (Inhibits B Cells), Complement Scavenging, Idiotypic Network, Treg Expansion, Cytokine Modulation
2IVIG vs SCIG — key differences?IVIG: IV, q3-4w, High Peak, Systemic SEs; SCIG: SC, Weekly, Steady State, Local SEs, Home Admin
3. Anti-TNF monitoring?Mandatory LTBI Screen (IGRA/TST) Pre-Tx, HBV/HIV Screen, LFT/CBC q3-6m; Monitor for TB Reactivation, Infections, Malignancy, Demyelination, HF
4. Rituximab — key monitoring?CD19+ Count, IgG Levels, HBV DNA/HBsAg, PML (JCV)
5. Tocilizumab — key monitoring?LFT (ALT/AST ↑), Lipids (TG/TC ↑), Neutrophils, Platelets, CBC
6. JAK Inhibitors — class adverse effects?Herpes Zoster (↑↑), VTE (PE/DVT), MACE (CV), Lipids ↑, Cytopenias, Infections, Hepatotoxicity
7. S1P Modulators — first dose monitoring?Fingolimod: 6h ECG/BP Monitoring (Bradycardia, AV Block); Siponimod: CYP2C9/3A4 Genotype Required; Ozanimod: No 1st Dose Monitoring
8. BTK Inhibitors — class adverse effects?Ibrutinib: Atrial Fibrillation (↑↑), Bleeding, Hypertension, Diarrhoea; Acalabrutinib/Zanubrutinib: Less AFib/Bleeding
9. Venetoclax — TLS Prophylaxis?Hydration 3L/d, Allopurinol 300mg or Rasburicase, Monitor TLS Labs (K, Uric Acid, Phos, Ca) q4-8h
10. IVIG in ITP — dose & response?IVIG 1g/kg/d x2d (Total 2g/kg) → Platelet Rise in 24-48h, Duration 2-4 Weeks

🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"IVIG = Just Antibody Replacement"NO. Multiple Mechanisms: FcRn Blockade, FcγRIIb, Complement Scavenging, Idiotypic Network, Treg Expansion, Cytokine Modulation
"SCIG = Just Convenient IVIG"Different PK: Steady State IgG, Lower Peak, Less Systemic SEs, Home Admin; Not Interchangeable for All Indications (e.g., Acute ITP = IVIG Preferred)
"All Anti-TNF = Same"NO. Infliximab (Chimeric) > Immunogenicity, Certolizumab (No Fc) = Pregnancy Safe, Etanercept (Fusion Protein) = Lower TB Risk than Monoclonal
"Rituximab = Only B-Cell Depletion"NO. Also Hypogammaglobulinaemia, VZV Reactivation, HBV Reactivation, PML (JCV), Late-Onset Neutropenia
"JAK Inhibitors = All Same"NO. Tofacitinib (JAK1/3), Baricitinib (JAK1/2), Upadacitinib/Filgotinib (JAK1 Selective) — Different Selectivity, Dosing, Adverse Profiles
"S1P Modulators = All Same"NO. Fingolimod: 6h 1st Dose Obs, Bradycardia; Siponimod: CYP2C9/3A4 Genotype; Ozanimod/Ponesimod: No 1st Dose Monitor
"BTK Inhibitors = All Same"NO. Ibrutinib: ↑ AFib, Bleeding; Acalabrutinib/Zanubrutinib: Less AFib/Bleeding, Different CYP3A4 Interaction
"S1P Modulators = Lymphopenia = Good"NO. Lymphopenia = Mechanism, But Infection Risk ↑, VZV Reactivation Risk — Screen VZV IgG First
"Venetoclax = Just CLL Drug"NO. Also AML (Unfit + Aza), MCL, WM; TLS Risk (Allopurinol/Rasburicase Prophylaxis Essential)
"IVIG = No Adverse Effects"NO. Thrombosis, AKI, Haemolysis, Aseptic Meningitis, Anaphylaxis (IgA Def) — Monitor Creatinine, Platelets, Hb
Mnemonic: IMMUNE THERAPIES ESSENTIALS
IVIG: FcRn Blockade + FcγRIIb + Complement Scavenging + Idiotypic + Treg + Cytokine Mod → PID, CIDP, GBS, ITP, Kawasaki, Autoimmune
IVIG vs SCIG: IV = IV, Peak, q3-4w, Systemic SEs; SC = SC, Trough, Weekly, Local SEs, Home
Monoclonal Antibodies: Anti-TNF (TB Screen!), Anti-IL6R (LFT/Lipids), Anti-IL17/23 (TB Screen), Anti-CD20 (CD19/IgG/HBV/PML)
Mechanisms: Anti-TNF (TNFα Block), Anti-IL6R (IL-6R Block), Anti-IL17/23 (Th17 Block), Anti-CD20 (B-Cell Depletion), Anti-IL1 (IL-1R/IL-1β Block)
U (JAKi): JAK1/3 (Tofa), JAK1/2 (Bari), JAK1 (Upada/Filgo) → HZ↑↑, VTE, MACE, Lipids, Cytopenias
N (S1P Mod): Fingo (1st Dose 6h Obs), Siponi (CYP Genotype), Ozani/Ponesi (No 1st Dose Obs)
E (BTKi): Ibrutinib (AFib↑, Bleed), Acalabru/Zanu (Less AFib/Bleed)
T (Venetoclax): TLS Prophylaxis (Hydration 3L/d + Allo 300mg or Rasburicase)
T (Cytokines): G-CSF (Neutropenia), EPO (CKD Anaemia), TPO (ITP), IFN-α/β (MS, Hep C), GM-CSF
H (mAbs): Anti-TNF (Infliximab Chimeric, Ada Human, Certo PEGylated/Fab, Goli Human, Etanercept Fusion)
E (S1P): Fingo (S1P1,3,4,5), Siponi (1,5), Ozani (1,5), Ponesi (1) — Sequestration in LN
R (BTKi): Ibrutinib (Covalent, AFib/Bleed), Acalabrutinib (Reversible, Less AFib), Zanubrutinib (Reversible, Best AFib Profile)
R (Venetoclax): BCL-2 Inhibitor → Apoptosis → TLS Risk (Hydration + Allopurinol/Rasburicase)
A (Cellular): Treg (FOXP3, T1DM/Transplant), MSC (GvHD, Fistula, ARDS), CAR-T (CD19/BCMA)
A (CAR-T): CD19 (B-ALL, DLBCL, FL), BCMA (Myeloma) — CRS (Toci) + ICANS (Dex 1st)
P (TCR-T/TIL/NK): NY-ESO-1/MAGE-A4/KRAS TCR-T, TIL (Lifileucel Melanoma), NK (Allo/CAR-NK)
B (BiTEs): Blina (CD19xCD3), Tecla (BCMAxCD3), Tecli (GPRC5DxCD3), Talque (GPRC5DxCD3)
S (Monit): IVIG (IgG Trough, Renal, IgA), Tofa (CBC/LFT/Lipids/CK/VZV/TB), Bari (CBC/LFT/Lipids/CK/Lymph), Upada (CBC/LFT/Lipids/CK/CPK)
P (Venetoclax): TLS Prophylaxis = Hydration 3L/d + Allo 300mg or Rasburicase
I (SCIG): Home, Weekly, Steady IgG, Local SE, No Aseptic Meningitis
E (Etanercept): Only Fusion Protein (TNFR2-Fc), No Fc, Lowest TB Risk
T (Teprotumumab): IGF-1R Ab for TED (FDA/EMA Approved)
H (HLA): HLA-B15:02 (Carbamazepine), HLA-B57:01 (Abacavir), HLA-B*58:01 (Allopurinol)
E (Enzyme): TPMT (Aza/6-MP), NUDT15 (6-MP Asian), DPYD (5-FU), CYP2C19 (Clopidogrel), CYP2D6 (Codeine/Tamoxifen)
R (Rituximab): Chimeric (Mouse-Human), CD20, HypoIgG, PML, HBV, VZV
A (Abatacept): CTLA4-Ig, Blocks CD28-B7, RA, JIA, Transplant, LTE
P (Pegfilgrastim): G-CSF, Pegylated, 6mg Single Dose/Cycle
I (Ibrutinib): BTK Covalent Inhibitor, AFib↑, Bleed↑, CYP3A4 Substrate
S (Siponimod): S1P1,5 Selective, CYP2C9/3A4 Genotype, No 1st Dose Bradycardia
A (Acalabrutinib): BTK Reversible, Less AFib/Bleed, CYP3A4 Substrate
N (Natalizumab): α4 Integrin, PML (JCV Ab+), JCV Ab Screen Mandatory
E (Eculizumab): C5 Inhibitor, aHUS, PNH, gMG
Q (Quiz): FCPS/MRCP: Know Mechanisms, Monitoring, SEs, Contraindications, Dosing, Interactions

💬 Exam Answer Modes

FormatPromptKey Points
Long Essay"Describe the mechanisms of action, indications, and monitoring of IVIG therapy."FcRn Blockade, FcγRIIb, Complement Scavenging, Idiotypic Network, Treg Expansion, Indications (PID, Neurological, Haematological, Autoimmune, Transplant), IVIG vs SCIG, Monitoring, Adverse Effects
Short Note"JAK inhibitors — mechanism, indications, adverse effects, monitoring."JAK1/3 (Tofa), JAK1/2 (Bari), JAK1 (Upada/Filgo) → JAK-STAT Inhibition; Indications (RA, PsA, AD, UC); SEs: HZ, VTE, MACE, Lipids, Cytopenias; Monitoring: CBC, LFT, Lipids, CK, VZV IgG, TB, CVD Risk
Viva"Patient on tofacitinib develops herpes zoster. Management?"Hold JAKi, Treat with Antivirals (Valaciclovir 1g TDS 7d), Restart JAKi after Resolution if Benefit > Risk, Counsel on Vaccination (Shingrix Pre-Tx)
Ward Round"Patient on adalimumab for Crohn's develops TB. Management?"Stop Adalimumab, Start Anti-TB Therapy (Standard 4-Drug Regimen), Restart Biologic after 2 Months TB Treatment if Benefit > Risk, Discuss Alternative Biologics (Vedolizumab, Ustekinumab)
Last-Night"IVIG: FcRn/FcγRIIb/Complement/Idiotypic/Treg → PID/CIDP/GBS/ITP/Kawasaki. SCIG: Home/Weekly. Anti-TNF: TB Screen Mandatory. Rituximab: CD19/IgG/HBV/PML. Tocilizumab: LFT/Lipids/Neutrophils. JAKi: HZ↑↑/VTE/MACE/Lipids/Cytopenias. S1P: Fingo(6hObs), Siponi(CYP Genotype). BTKi: Ibrutinib(AFib↑), Acalabru(Zanubrutinib). Venetoclax: TLS Prophy (Hydration+Allo/Rasburicase). Cytokines: G-CSF/EPO/TPO/IFN/GM-CSF. CAR-T: CRS/ICANS."Compressed.

📌 Summary

  • IVIG/SCIG: Multiple mechanisms (FcRn, FcγRIIb, Complement, Idiotypic, Treg, Cytokines); IVIG: IV q3-4w, SCIG: SC Weekly, Home; Indications: PID, Neurological, Haematological, Autoimmune, Transplant
  • Monoclonal Antibodies: Anti-TNF (TB Screen Mandatory), Anti-IL-6R (LFT/Lipids/Neutrophils), Anti-IL-17/23 (TB Screen), Anti-IL-1, Anti-CD20 (CD19/IgG/HBV/PML), Anti-IL-4/13 (Eosinophilia), Anti-Integrin (Natalizumab: JCV/PML)
  • JAK Inhibitors: Tofacitinib (JAK1/3), Baricitinib (JAK1/2), Upadacitinib/Filgotinib (JAK1); HZ↑↑, VTE, MACE, Lipids↑, Cytopenias; CBC, LFT, Lipids, CK, VZV IgG, TB Screen, CVD Risk
  • S1P Modulators: Fingolimod (6h 1st Dose Obs), Siponimod (CYP Genotype), Ozanimod/Ponesimod (No 1st Dose Obs); Lymphocyte Sequestration in LN; Bradycardia, AV Block, Macular Edema, Infections
  • BTK Inhibitors: Ibrutinib (AFib↑, Bleeding↑), Acalabrutinib/Zanubrutinib (Less AFib/Bleed); CYP3A4 Substrate
  • Venetoclax: BCL-2 Inhibitor, TLS Prophylaxis (Hydration 3L/d + Allopurinol 300mg or Rasburicase)
  • Cytokines: G-CSF (Neutropenia), EPO (CKD Anaemia), TPO (ITP), IFN-α/β (MS, Hepatitis), GM-CSF
  • Cellular Therapies: Treg (FOXP3, T1DM/Transplant), MSC (GvHD, Fistula, ARDS), CAR-T (CD19/BCMA, CRS/ICANS → Tocilizumab/Dex), TCR-T/TIL/NK/BiTEs
  • Biosimilars: Extrapolation, Interchangeability, Immunogenicity Monitoring

❓ MCQs (10)

  1. IVIG mechanism — FcRn blockade leads to:

A. ↑ IgG Synthesis B. ↑ Catabolism of Endogenous IgG (Autoantibodies) C. ↓ B Cell Production D. ↑ Complement Activation

Answer: B. FcRn Saturation → ↓ IgG Recycling → ↑ Catabolism of Pathogenic Autoantibodies.

  1. SCIG vs IVIG — key advantage of SCIG?

A. Higher Peak IgG B. Home Self-Administration, Stable Trough Levels C. Less Frequent Dosing D. Lower Cost

Answer: B. SCIG = Home Self-Administration, Stable Steady-State IgG, Less Systemic Adverse Effects.

  1. Anti-TNF — mandatory pre-treatment screening?

A. HIV Only B. LTBI (IGRA/TST) + HBV C. HCV Only D. VZV IgG Only

Answer: B. LTBI Screen (IGRA/TST) + HBV Screen Mandatory Before Anti-TNF.

  1. Rituximab — key monitoring parameter not required?

A. CD19+ B Cell Count B. CD4+ T Cell Count C. IgG Levels D. HBV DNA/HBsAg

Answer: B. Rituximab Depletes B Cells (CD19+), Not T Cells (CD4+). Monitor CD19+, IgG, HBV.

  1. Tocilizumab — laboratory abnormality requiring monitoring?

A. Hyperkalaemia B. Hyperlipidaemia (TG/TC ↑) & Neutropenia C. Hypocalcaemia D. Hypernatraemia

Answer: B. Tocilizumab → ↑ Lipids (TG/TC), ↓ Neutrophils, ↑ LFT.

  1. JAK Inhibitor — class-specific adverse effect?

A. Hypoglycaemia B. Herpes Zoster (↑↑ Incidence) C. Hyperkalaemia D. Hypermagnesaemia

Answer: B. JAK Inhibitors → ↑ Herpes Zoster (2-3x Risk).

  1. Fingolimod — first-dose monitoring?

A. LFT B. ECG/BP for 6 Hours (Bradycardia, AV Block) C. Lipids D. CBC

Answer: B. 6-Hour Cardiac Monitoring Post-First Dose (Bradycardia, AV Block).

  1. Ibrutinib — characteristic adverse effect?

A. Hyperglycaemia B. Atrial Fibrillation & Bleeding C. Hypothyroidism D. Hyperkalaemia

Answer: B. Ibrutinib → ↑ Atrial Fibrillation (2-3x), ↑ Major Bleeding.

  1. Venetoclax — tumour lysis syndrome prophylaxis?

A. Hydration Only B. Hydration 3L/Day + Allopurinol 300mg or Rasburicase C. Rasburicase Only D. Dialysis Prophylaxis

Answer: B. Hydration 3L/Day + Allopurinol 300mg (or Rasburicase).

  1. Rituximab — PML risk factor?

A. Low CD4 B. Prolonged/CD19+ Depletion, Rituximab >1 Year, Prior Immunosuppression C. High IgG D. Low CD8

Answer: B. Prolonged B-Cell Depletion, Prior Immunosuppression, Rituximab Duration.

  1. S1P Modulator — no first-dose cardiac monitoring required?

A. Fingolimod B. Siponimod C. Ozanimod D. Ponesimod

Answer: C. Ozanimod (and Ponesimod) — No First Dose Cardiac Monitoring Required.

📋 SBAs (10)

  1. Patient on infliximab for Crohn's develops fever, cough, weight loss 3 months after starting. CXR: upper lobe cavitation. Most likely?

A. Crohn's Flare B. TB Reactivation C. Fungal Pneumonia D. Lymphoma

Answer: B. Anti-TNF → TB Reactivation (Typically 3-12 Months Post-Start).

  1. Patient on tofacitinib 5mg BD for RA develops Herpes Zoster. Management?

A. Stop Tofacitinib Permanently B. Hold Tofacitinib, Treat with Valaciclovir, Restart After Resolution C. Continue Tofacitinib, Add Aciclovir D. Switch to Biologic

Answer: B. Hold JAKi, Treat HZ, Restart When Resolved if Benefit > Risk.

  1. CLL patient starting venetoclax + obinutuzumab. WBC 80x10⁹/L. TLS Risk?

A. Low B. High (Tumour Burden + Venetoclax) C. Moderate D. None

Answer: B. High Tumour Burden + Venetoclax = High TLS Risk → Hydration + Allopurinol/Rasburicase.

  1. MS Patient on Fingolimod. Day 1 Post-First Dose. HR 42, BP 90/60. Action?

A. Continue B. Hold, Cardiac Monitoring, Atropine if Symptomatic C. Switch to Siponimod D. Reduce Dose

Answer: B. First-Dose Bradycardia/AV Block → Hold, Monitor 6h, Atropine if Symptomatic.

  1. Patient on Rituximab for RA develops Hypogammaglobulinaemia (IgG 3.5 g/L) with Recurrent Infections. Management?

A. Stop Rituximab B. IVIG Replacement (IgG <4 + Recurrent Infections) C. Increase Rituximab Dose D. Switch to Tocilizumab

Answer: B. IVIG Replacement if IgG <4 g/L + Recurrent Infections.

🧠 Core Concept: Immunology in Special Situations

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Special Situations in Immunology
↓
Immunosenescence & Inflammageing Age-Related Changes
Pregnancy Immunology Maternal-Fetal Tolerance, Autoimmunity, RH Disease
Critical Illness Immunology Sepsis Hyperinflammation → Immunoparalysis
Obesity & Metabolic Syndrome Metaflammation, Adipose Immunity, Insulin Resistance
Microbiome-Immune Interactions Dysbiosis, GALT, Trained Immunity, FMT
Vaccinology Platforms, Schedules, Hesitancy, Emerging

1️⃣ Immunosenescence & Inflammageing

Age-Related Immune Remodelling

ComponentAge-Related ChangeClinical Consequence
ThymusThymic Involution (Fatty Replacement) → ↓ Naive T Cell Output↓ Naive T Cells, ↓ TCR Diversity, ↓ Response to Novel Antigens (Vaccines, New Infections)
T Cells↓ Naive (CD45RA+), ↑ Memory (CD45RO+), ↓ CD28, ↑ Senescence (CD57+, KLRG1+), ↑ Tregs↓ Response to Novel Pathogens/Vaccines, ↑ Autoreactivity, ↑ Latent Virus Reactivation (VZV, CMV)
B Cells↓ Naive B Cells, ↓ Class Switch Recombination, ↓ Somatic Hypermutation↓ Vaccine Response (Lower Affinity/Avidity Antibodies), ↓ New Antigen Response
Innate ImmunityNeutrophil Dysfunction (↓ Chemotaxis, Phagocytosis, NETosis), Macrophage Dysfunction, ↓ NK Cytotoxicity↑ Bacterial/Fungal Infections, ↓ Tumour Surveillance
Inflammation"Inflammageing" — Chronic Low-Grade Inflammation (↑ IL-6, TNF-α, CRP, IL-1β, IFN-γ)Frailty, Sarcopenia, Atherosclerosis, Neurodegeneration, Insulin Resistance, Cancer
CMV SeropositivityAccelerates Immunosenescence — Massive CMV-Specific T Cell Expansions (Memory Inflation)↑ Mortality, ↓ Vaccine Response, ↑ Frailty

Clinical Implications

DomainImpact
VaccinationReduced Response to ALL Vaccines; Higher Doses/Adjuvants Needed (High-Dose Flu, Adjuvanted Shingrix, High-Dose Hep B); Repeated Doses
Infections↑ Respiratory Infections (Influenza, Pneumococcal, COVID-19, RSV), Zoster Reactivation, UTIs, Sepsis
Cancer↓ Immune Surveillance → ↑ Incidence, ↓ Immunotherapy Efficacy (Checkpoint Inhibitors)
Autoimmunity↑ Late-Onset Autoimmune Disease (RA, PMR, GCA, AIHA)

Vaccination in Elderly (UK Schedule)

VaccineRecommendation
Seasonal InfluenzaAnnual — High-Dose Quadrivalent (HD-QIV) or Adjuvanted (aQIV) Preferred >65y
PneumococcalPCV20 (Single Dose) OR PCV15 → PPV23 (1 Year Later)
Herpes ZosterShingrix (Recombinant zoster vaccine) — 2 Doses 2-6 Months Apart (Preferred > Zostavax)
COVID-19Boosters Per JCVI (Seasonal, Variants)
RSVArexvy/Abrysvo (New) — ≥60y (Shared Clinical Decision)
PertussisTdap Booster (If Not in Last 10y)

2️⃣ Immunology of Pregnancy

Maternal-Fetal Tolerance

MechanismDescription
HLA-G (Trophoblast)Non-classical HLA — Binds ILT2/LILRB1 on NK/T Cells → Inhibition
HLA-EBinds NKG2A/CD94 on NK Cells → Inhibition
PD-L1/PD-L2 (Trophoblast)Binds PD-1 on T Cells → Inhibition
IDO (Tryptophan Catabolism)Local Tryptophan Depletion → T Cell Anergy/Apoptosis
Treg ExpansionFoxP3+ Tregs ↑ in Decidua → IL-10, TGF-β, IL-35
HLA-C (Paternal)KIR-HLA Interactions on uNK Cells → Licensing/Inhibition Balance
Key: Semi-Allogeneic Fetus Tolerated — "Immunological Paradox of Pregnancy"

Autoimmune Disease in Pregnancy

DiseasePregnancy ImpactManagement
SLEFlare Risk (2nd/3rd Trimester, Postpartum); Lupus Nephritis → Preterm, Pre-eclampsiaHCQ Continued (Safe), Avoid MMF/Mycophenolate (Teratogenic), AZA/Steroids Safe, Belimumab (Limited Data)
APSHigh Risk Thrombosis/Fetal LossLMWH (Enoxaparin) Prophylactic/Therapeutic + Aspirin 75-150mg throughout
RAImprovement (2nd/3rd Trimester), Postpartum Flare (90%)Continue HCQ/SSZ, Stop MTX/LEF/TOFA/JAKi (Teratogenic), Certolizumab Preferred Biologic (No Fc Transfer)
IBD (CD/UC)Flare Risk (If Active at Conception)Continue Mesalamine/Thiopurines/Anti-TNF (Certolizumab/Infiximab/Adalimumab Safe)
MSReduced Relapses (3rd Trimester), Postpartum Rebound (3m)Continue Glatiramer/Natalizumab/Ofatumumab, Stop Fingolimod/Siponimod/Ozanimod/Ponesimod (Teratogenic)
T1DMStrict Glycaemic Control Pre-Conception → HbA1c <48 mmol/molInsulin Pump/CGM, Folic Acid 5mg, Aspirin 75mg (Pre-eclampsia Prophylaxis)

Drug Safety in Pregnancy (Immunology-Relevant)

DrugPregnancy Category (UK/BNF)Notes
HydroxychloroquineSafe (Continue)Strongly Recommended in SLE
AzathioprineSafe (Continue)Monitor FBC, LFT
Azathioprine (Pregnancy)Category D?BNF: Safe (No Teratogenicity Data)
MethotrexateContraindicated (Category X)Stop 3-6 Months Pre-Conception
LeflunomideContraindicated (Category X)Washout + Cholestyramine Pre-Conception
Mycophenolate (MMF)Contraindicated (Category X)STOP 6 Weeks Pre-Conception
CyclophosphamideContraindicated (Category X)High Teratogenicity
Biologics (TNFi)Certolizumab = Safe (No Fc); Others: Cross Placenta (IgG1) 3rd TrimesterStop Infliximab/Adalimumab/Golimumab ~20-24w; Certolizumab Continued
Biologics (Non-TNF)Rituximab (Contraindicated 3rd Trimester)B-Cell Depletion in Fetus
JAK InhibitorsContraindicatedTeratogenic (Animal Data)
CorticosteroidsSafe (Prednisolone <20mg/d)Cross Placenta (Inactivated by Placental 11β-HSD2)
IVIGSafeUsed in ITP, APS, Kawasaki

Rhesus Disease (Haemolytic Disease of Fetus & Newborn — HDFN)

FeatureDetail
PathogenesisRhD-Negative Mother → Sensitisation (Feto-Maternal Haemorrhage) → Anti-D IgG → Crosses Placenta → Haemolysis of RhD+ve Fetus
PreventionAnti-D IgG Prophylaxis: 28w + 34w (Routine), Post-Delivery (72h), Sensitising Events (Bleeding, Amnio, Trauma)
MonitoringMaternal Anti-D Titre (q4w 28-32w, q2w 28-34w), MCA Doppler (MCA-PSV >1.5 MoM = Anaemia)
TreatmentIntrauterine Transfusion (IUT), Phototherapy, Exchange Transfusion, IVIG (Adjunct)

Vaccination in Pregnancy (UK)

VaccineTimingSafety
Pertussis (Tdap)16-32 Weeks (Optimal 20-32w)Safe — Transfers IgG to Fetus
InfluenzaAny Trimester (Seasonal)Safe (Inactivated)
COVID-19Any TrimesterSafe (mRNA Preferred)
RSV (Abrysvo)28-36 WeeksSafe (Maternal Immunisation → Infant Protection)
Live Vaccines (MMR, Varicella, BCG, Yellow Fever, Oral Typhoid)ContraindicatedTheoretical Risk to Fetus

3️⃣ Immunology of Critical Illness

Sepsis Immunodynamics — Biphasic Model

⬇ Clinical Pathway
Sepsis Onset
↓
Hyperinflammatory Phase Hours-Days 1-3
↓
Cytokine Storm IL-6, TNF-α, IL-1β, IL-8, HMGB1, PAMPs/DAMPs
↓
Endothelial Activation Coagulopathy, Capillary Leak, Vasodilation
↓
Immunoparalysis Phase Days 3-7+
↓
Lymphopenia HLA-DR↓ on Monocytes PD-1/PD-L1↑, TIM-3↑, LAG-3↑
↓
Treg Expansion IL-10↑, TGF-β↑
↓
Secondary Infections Nosocomial, Fungal, Viral Reactivation

Immunoparalysis Biomarkers

BiomarkerSignificanceThreshold
mHLA-DR (Monocyte HLA-DR)Gold Standard for Immunoparalysis<30% (or <5000 Ab/C) = Severe Immunoparalysis
Lymphocyte Count<800/μL or <1000/μLSustained Lymphopenia = Poor Outcome
PD-1 / PD-L1T Cell Exhaustion↑ Expression = Exhaustion
IL-10 / IL-6 RatioAnti-inflammatory DominanceIL-10/IL-6 >1 = Immunosuppression
CD4+ T Cell Count<400/μLPredicts Secondary Infection

Immune Modulation Therapies (Investigational)

TherapyTargetStatus
IFN-γRestores HLA-DR, ↑ PhagocytosisPhase II/III (IMMUNOSEP, IFNg-SEPSIS)
GM-CSFMyeloid Differentiation, PhagocytosisPhase II (NCT02361528)
IL-7T Cell Homeostasis, LymphopoiesisPhase II (REVIVE, CYCLE)
Anti-PD-1/PD-L1Reverse T Cell ExhaustionCase Reports, Small Trials
IL-15NK/CD8+ Memory ExpansionPreclinical

Haemophagocytic Lymphohistiocytosis (HLH) / Macrophage Activation Syndrome (MAS)

FeatureDetail
PathogenesisUncontrolled T/NK activation → Cytokine storm (IFN-γ, IL-6, IL-18, IL-10, CXCL9/10) → Macrophage activation → Phagocytosis of blood cells (Haemophagocytosis)
TriggersPrimary (Familial): PRF1, UNC13D, STX11, STXBP2, RAB27A perforin defects; Secondary: Infection (EBV, CMV), Malignancy (Lymphoma), Autoimmune (SLE, sJIA = MAS), Drugs
HLH-2004 Criteria≥5 of 8: Fever, Splenomegaly, Cytopenias (≥2 lineages), Hypertriglyceridaemia / Hypofibrinogenaemia, Haemophagocytosis (BM/Spleen/LN), Low/absent NK activity, Ferritin ≥500 µg/L (often >>10,000), sCD25 (sIL-2Rα) ≥2400 U/mL
HScoreRisk score for secondary HLH (0-266): Temperature, Organomegaly, Cytopenias, Ferritin, Triglycerides, Fibrinogen, AST, Haemophagocytosis, Immunosuppression; ≥169 = 93% prob. HLH; ≥200 = 99% prob.
TreatmentHLH-94 Protocol: Dexamethasone + Etoposide + Intrathecal Methotrexate; Anakinra (IL-1Ra) for MAS/sJIA; Ruxolitinib (JAK1/2i) for refractory; Eculizumab (C5i) for CAPS-associated; HSCT for familial/refractory

4️⃣ Immunology of Obesity & Metabolic Syndrome

Metaflammation (Metabolic Inflammation)

FeatureMechanism
Adipose Tissue ExpansionHypertrophy → Hypoxia → Necrosis → Crown-Like Structures (Macrophage Crowns)
Macrophage PolarisationM1 (Pro-inflammatory) Dominance in VAT (Visceral Adipose Tissue) → TNF-α, IL-6, IL-1β, MCP-1
Adipokine DysregulationLeptin ↑ (Pro-inflammatory), Adiponectin ↓ (Anti-inflammatory, Insulin Sensitising)
Insulin ResistanceJNK/IKKβ/NF-κB Activation → Serine Phosphorylation of IRS-1 → Impaired Insulin Signalling
Gut-Liver AxisDysbiosis → LPS/TLR4 → Kupffer Cell Activation → Hepatic Inflammation (NAFLD/NASH)

Immune Consequences of Obesity

DomainImpact
Infection↑ Post-Op Infections, Wound Complications, Influenza Severity, COVID-19 Severity
Vaccine ResponseImpaired (Lower Antibody Titres, Faster Waning) — Hepatitis B, Influenza, COVID-19
Cancer↑ ESCC, HCC, Colorectal, Endometrial, Breast, Pancreatic (Chronic Inflammation, Insulin/IGF-1)
Autoimmunity↑ RA, PsA, SLE, MS, Hashimoto's (Adipokines, Leptin, Inflammasome)
Vaccine ResponseReduced Seroconversion (Hb <10 → Lower Titres, Faster Waning)

5️⃣ Microbiome-Immune Interactions

Gut-Associated Lymphoid Tissue (GALT)

ComponentFunction
Peyer's PatchesInductive Sites — IgA Class Switch, T Cell Priming
Isolated Lymphoid FolliclesAntigen Sampling (M Cells)
Lamina PropriaEffector Site — IgA+ Plasma Cells, Trm (Tissue-Resident Memory T Cells), ILC3
Mesenteric Lymph NodesDrainage → Systemic Immune Priming

Microbiome-Immune Crosstalk

MechanismEffect
SCFAs (Butyrate, Propionate, Acetate)HDAC Inhibition → Treg Expansion, Barrier Integrity, Anti-inflammatory
Bile Acid MetabolismFXR/FXR Activation → Metabolic Regulation, Immune Modulation
Tryptophan MetabolismAhR Ligands (Indoles) → IL-22, IL-17, Barrier Function
Bile Acid Transformation7α-Dehydroxylation → Secondary Bile Acids → TGR5/FXR
Molecular MimicryMicrobial Peptides ↔ Self-Antigens → Cross-Reactivity (Molecular Mimicry)

Dysbiosis & Disease

ConditionMicrobiome SignatureImmune Mechanism
IBD (CD/UC)↓ Diversity, ↓ Faecalibacterium, ↑ EnterobacteriaceaeLoss of SCFAs, Barrier Defect, Th1/Th17
RA↑ Prevotella copri, ↓ DiversityMolecular Mimicry, Citrullination
T1DM↓ Diversity, ↓ Butyrate ProducersLoss of Tolerance, β-Cell Autoimmunity
MS↓ Clostridia, ↑ AkkermansiaTh17/Treg Imbalance, BBB Disruption
Obesity/T2DM↓ Diversity, ↑ Firmicutes/Bacteroidetes RatioEndotoxaemia (LPS) → Metaflammation
Allergy/Asthma↓ Diversity (Early Life), ↓ Farm ExposureHygiene Hypothesis, ↓ Treg Induction

Trained Immunity (Innate Immune Memory)

ConceptDescription
DefinitionEpigenetic Reprogramming of Innate Immune Cells (Monocytes, NK Cells) → Enhanced Response to Secondary Stimulus
InducersBCG, β-Glucan, Measles Vaccine, BCG Scarification
Epigenetic ChangesH3K4me3, H3K27ac at Promoters of Inflammatory Genes (IL-6, TNF-α, IL-1β)
Clinical RelevanceBCG → ↓ Neonatal Mortality, BCG → ↓ Respiratory Infections, BCG → ↓ COVID-19 Severity (Debated)

Faecal Microbiota Transplantation (FMT)

IndicationEfficacy
Recurrent C. difficile Infection (rCDI)>90% Cure Rate (Superior to Vancomycin)
IBD (UC)Remission Induction (Modest, Donor-Dependent)
Obesity/Metabolic SyndromeExperimental (Improved Insulin Sensitivity)
Autism/NeuropsychiatricExperimental (Gut-Brain Axis)

6️⃣ Vaccinology

Vaccine Platforms

PlatformMechanismExamplesAdvantagesLimitations
Live AttenuatedReplicating, Weakened PathogenMMR, Varicella, BCG, Oral Polio, Rotavirus, Yellow FeverStrong Cellular + Humoral, Long-Lasting, Single DoseContraindicated in Immunocompromised, Pregnancy; Cold Chain
Inactivated (Killed)Non-Replicating PathogenInfluenza (IIV), Hepatitis A, Polio (IPV), Rabies, Cholera, Pertussis (wP)Safe in Immunocompromised, StableWeaker Immunogenicity, Multiple Doses, Adjuvants Needed
Subunit/ProteinPurified AntigenHepatitis B, HPV, Pertussis (aP), Meningococcal (MenACWY), ShingrixSafe, Defined AntigensMultiple Doses, Adjuvants Needed
ToxoidInactivated ToxinDiphtheria, TetanusNeutralising AntibodiesBoosters Needed
ConjugatePolysaccharide + Carrier ProteinHib, MenACWY, PCV13/15/20, TyphoidT-Cell Dependent Response in InfantsComplex Manufacturing
Viral VectorReplication-Deficient Virus Delivers Antigen GeneAstraZeneca (ChAdOx1), J&J (Ad26), Sputnik V (Ad26+Ad5), Ebola (rVSV-ZEBOV)Strong CD8+ T Cell, Single Dose PossiblePre-Existing Vector Immunity, Rare TTS (VITT)
mRNA (LNP)mRNA → Host Translation → AntigenPfizer/BioNTech (BNT162b2), Moderna (mRNA-1273)Rapid Development, Strong CD4/CD8/Ab, No Live VirusCold Chain (-70°C to -20°C), Reactogenicity, Myocarditis (Rare)
DNA PlasmidDNA → Nucleus → mRNA → ProteinZyCoV-D (India), Inovio (INO-4800)Stable, No Cold ChainLower Immunogenicity (Historically), Electroporation Needed
Protein Subunit (Adjuvanted)Recombinant Protein + AdjuvantNovavax (NVX-CoV2373), Sanofi/GSK (VidPrevtyn)Safe, No Genetic Material, Strong AbAdjuvant Dependency

Malaria Vaccine (RTS,S/AS01 — Mosquirix)

FeatureDetail
TargetPlasmodium falciparum Circumsporozoite Protein (CSP)
PlatformRecombinant Protein (CSP-HBsAg fusion) + AS01 Adjuvant
Schedule4 Doses: 5, 6, 7 Months + Booster at 18 Months (0-1-2-20m)
Efficacy~30-40% against Clinical Malaria (4 years); ~50% in first year; ~30% against Severe Malaria
WHO RecommendationBroad Implementation in Sub-Saharan Africa (2021) — Pilot Rollout: Ghana, Kenya, Malawi
ImpactReduces Severe Malaria Hospitalisations; Cost-Effective alongside ITNs, SMC, IRS
LimitationsWaning Immunity (Requires Booster); Not 100% Protective; Cold Chain Required

|### UK Immunisation Schedule (Key Points)

AgeVaccines
8 Weeks6-in-1 (DTaP/IPV/Hib/HepB), Rotavirus, MenB, PCV
12 Weeks6-in-1 (2nd), Rotavirus (2nd), PCV (2nd)
16 Weeks6-in-1 (3rd), MenB (2nd)
1 YearHib/MenC, MMR (1st), PCV (Booster), MenB (Booster)
3y 4mMMR (2nd), 4-in-1 (DTaP/IPV Booster)
12-13y (Girls/Boys)HPV (2 Doses, 6-24m Apart)
14yMenACWY, Td/IPV (Booster)
≥65yFlu (Annual, HD/aQIV), Pneumococcal (PCV20), Shingrix, COVID, RSV
PregnancyTdap (16-32w), Flu, COVID, RSV (28-36w)

Vaccine Contraindications & Precautions

ContraindicationVaccines Affected
Anaphylaxis to Previous Dose/ComponentAll
Severe ImmunodeficiencyLive Vaccines (MMR, Varicella, BCG, Rotavirus, Yellow Fever, LAIV, Oral Typhoid)
PregnancyLive Vaccines (MMR, Varicella, BCG, Yellow Fever, LAIV)
Severe Egg AllergyInfluenza (Cell-Based/Recombinant OK), Yellow Fever
Guillain-Barré (Within 6w of Flu Vaccine)Influenza (Precaution)
Thrombocytopenia/CoagulopathyIM Injections (Caution), Intranasal/SC Preferred

Vaccine Hesitancy / Equity

DimensionStrategy
ConfidenceTransparent Communication, Trusted Messengers (HCPs, Community Leaders), Address Myths (Fertility, DNA, Microchips)
ComplacencyRisk Communication, Remind Severity, Reminders/Recalls
ConvenienceAccessible Locations (Pharmacies, Community Centres), Flexible Hours, Walk-Ins, Co-Administration
EquityTargeted Outreach (Underserved, Ethnic Minorities, Homeless, Learning Disabilities), Multilingual Materials, Cultural Sensitivity

⚡ FCPS/MRCP High-Yield Summary

TopicKey Points
ImmunosenescenceThymic Involution → ↓ Naive T Cells, ↑ Memory/Senescent T Cells, Inflammageing (↑ IL-6, TNF, CRP), CMV Accelerates; Vaccine Response ↓ → High-Dose/Adjuvanted Vaccines
Pregnancy ImmunologyMaternal-Fetal Tolerance: HLA-G, HLA-E, PD-L1, IDO, Tregs; Autoimmune in Pregnancy: SLE (Flare Risks, HCQ Safe), APS (LMWH+Aspirin), RA (Improves, Certolizumab Safe), IBD (Continue Biologics), MS (Relapse Postpartum)
Drug Safety in PregnancyHCQ Safe, AZA Safe, MTX/LEF/MMF/CYC Contraindicated, TNFi: Certolizumab Safe (No Fc), Others Stop 20-24w, JAKi Contraindicated, Rituximab Avoid 3rd Trimester
RHDAnti-D Prophylaxis (28/34w, Post-Delivery, Sensitising Events), MCA Doppler, IUT/Phototherapy/Exchange
Vaccines in PregnancyTdap (16-32w), Flu (Any Trimester), COVID, RSV (28-36w); Live Vaccines Contraindicated
Critical IllnessHyperinflammatory → Immunoparalysis; mHLA-DR <30% = Immunoparalysis; Biomarkers: mHLA-DR, Lymphopenia, PD-1, IL-10; Therapies: IFN-γ, GM-CSF, IL-7 (Experimental)
ObesityMetaflammation: VAT → M1 Macrophages → TNF/IL-6/IL-1β → Insulin Resistance; Vaccine Response ↓; ↑ Infection/Cancer/Autoimmunity Risk
MicrobiomeSCFAs → Treg ↑, Barrier ↑; Dysbiosis: IBD, RA, T1DM, MS, Obesity; Trained Immunity (BCG, β-Glucan → Epigenetic Reprogramming); FMT (rCDI >90%)
VaccinesPlatforms: Live Attenuated, Inactivated, Subunit, Conjugate, Viral Vector, mRNA, Protein Subunit; Cold Chain (mRNA: -70°C/-20°C); Contraindications: Live in Immunocompromised/Pregnancy
UK Schedule8/12/16w: 6-in-1, Rotavirus, MenB, PCV; 1yr: MMR, Hib/MenC, PCV, MenB; 3y4m: MMR, 4-in-1; 12-13y: HPV; 14y: MenACWY, Td/IPV; ≥65: Flu (HD/aQIV), PPV/PCV20, Shingrix, RSV
Vaccine Hesitancy3 Cs: Confidence (Trust), Complacency (Risk Perception), Convenience (Access); Equity: Targeted Outreach, Multilingual, Cultural Safety

🎤 Viva Questions (Expected Answers)

#QuestionExpected Answer
1What is immunosenescence?Age-related immune remodelling: Thymic involution → ↓ Naive T cells, ↑ Memory/Senescent T Cells, ↓ TCR Diversity, Inflammageing (↑ IL-6, TNF, CRP), CMV Acceleration
2Why are vaccines less effective in elderly?↓ Naive T/B Cells, ↓ TCR/BCR Diversity, Impaired DC Function, Inflammageing → Poor Germinal Centre Response → Lower Affinity/Avidity, Shorter Duration
3What vaccines are recommended for >65y in UK?Flu (High-Dose/Adjuvanted), Pneumococcal (PCV20), Shingrix (RZV), COVID Boosters, RSV (Arexvy/Abrysvo), Pneumococcal (PCV20)
4How does pregnancy affect SLE?Flare Risk (2nd/3rd Trimester, Postpartum); Lupus Nephritis → ↑ Preterm/Pre-eclampsia; HCQ Continued (Safe), Avoid MMF/Mycophenolate
5Which biologic is safe in pregnancy?Certolizumab Pegol (PEGylated Fab', No Fc Transfer) → Safe Throughout Pregnancy
6What is immunoparalysis?Late Sepsis Phase: Lymphopenia, mHLA-DR <30% on Monocytes, ↑ PD-1/PD-L1, ↑ Tregs, ↑ IL-10 → Secondary Infections, Poor Outcome
7Biomarker for sepsis immunoparalysis?mHLA-DR on Monocytes <30% (or <5000 Ab/C) — Best Biomarker
8How does obesity cause insulin resistance?VAT Macrophages → M1 Polarisation → TNF-α, IL-6, IL-1β → JNK/IKKβ/NF-κB → IRS-1 Serine Phosphorylation → Impaired Insulin Signalling
9What is trained immunity?Epigenetic Reprogramming of Innate Cells (Monocytes, NK) → Enhanced Response to Secondary Stimulus; Induced by BCG, β-Glucan, Measles Vaccine; H3K4me3/H3K27ac Epigenetic Marks
10mRNA vaccine mechanism?LNP-mRNA → Cytoplasm → Ribosome Translation → Antigen → MHC I/II Presentation → CD8+/CD4+ T Cell + Neutralising Antibody Response

🧩 Confusions & Mnemonics

ConfusionClarification
"Elderly shouldn't get live vaccines"Mostly True, but Shingrix (RZV) is RECOMBINANT (Non-Live) — Safe & Recommended >50y/≥18y Immunocompromised
"Pregnancy = Immunosuppression"NO. Selective Immune Modulation — Tolerance to Fetus + Preserved/Enhanced Innate Immunity (NK, Neutrophils); Th1→Th2 Shift
"All Biologics Contraindicated in Pregnancy"NO. Certolizumab (No Fc) = Safe Throughout; TNFi (except CZP) Stop 20-24w; Rituximab Avoid 3rd Trimester; JAKi Contraindicated
"Live Vaccines = Never in Immunocompromised"TRUE for Severe Immunodeficiency; BUT HIV on ART with CD4>200 → MMR/Varicella OK; RZV (Shingrix) = Non-Live = Safe
**"Immunoparalysis = Sepsis"NO. Late Phase of Sepsis; Hyperinflammatory Phase First (Cytokine Storm) → Then Immunoparalysis
"Obesity = Only Mechanical Problem"NO. Metaflammation — Adipose Tissue as Endocrine/Immune Organ → Chronic Inflammation → Insulin Resistance, Cancer, Autoimmunity
"Microbiome = Only Gut"NO. Skin, Lung, Oral, Vaginal, Urinary, Placental Microbiomes All Influence Systemic Immunity
"BCG = Only TB Vaccine"NO. BCG Induces Trained Immunity → Non-Specific Protection (Neonatal Mortality ↓, Respiratory Infections ↓)
"All Vaccines = Same Schedule Everywhere"NO. UK vs US vs WHO Differ (e.g., Varicella in US Schedule, BCG in UK High-Risk Only, MenB in UK/Canada, Not US Routine)
"mRNA Vaccines Alter DNA"NO. mRNA Never Enters Nucleus, No Reverse Transcriptase, Degraded in Days — No Genomic Integration
Mnemonic: SPECIAL SITUATIONS IMMUNOLOGY
Senescence: Thymic Involution → ↓ Naive T, ↑ Memory/Senescent, Inflammageing (IL-6/TNF/CRP), CMV Driver
Pregnancy: Tolerance (HLA-G/E, PD-L1, IDO, Treg) + Autoimmune (SLE Flare, APS→LMWH+Aspirin, RA→Improves, Certolizumab Safe)
Eligibility: Vaccines in Pregnancy (Tdap 16-32w, Flu/COVID Any Trimester, RSV 28-36w) — NO Live Vaccines
Critical Illness: Sepsis Biphasic (Hyperinflammatory → Immunoparalysis); mHLA-DR<30% = Immunoparalysis; IFN-γ/GM-CSF/IL-7 Experimental
Obesity: Metaflammation (VAT→M1 Macs→TNF/IL-6→Insulin Resistance); Vaccine Response ↓; Cancer/Autoimmunity Risk↑
Immune-Microbiome: GALT/Peyer's/M Cells, SCFAs→Treg↑/Barrier↑, Dysbiosis→IBD/RA/T1DM/MS, Trained Immunity (BCG/β-Glucan→Epigenetic)
Vaccinology: Platforms (Live/Inactivated/Subunit/Conjugate/Viral Vector/mRNA/DNA/Subunit+Adjuvant); UK Schedule (8/12/16w, 1y, 3y4m, 12-13y, 14y, ≥65y); Hesitancy (3Cs: Confidence/Complacency/Convenience)
RH Disease: Anti-D Prophylaxis (28/34w, Post-Delivery, Sensitising Events)
Special Groups: Immunocompromised (No Live), Elderly (High-Dose/Adjuvanted), Asplenia (Vaccines+Pen V), CKD/Dialysis (Hep B Double Dose), HIV (CD4>200→Live OK)

💬 Exam Answer Modes

FormatPromptKey Points
Long Essay"Discuss the immunological changes with ageing and their impact on vaccination strategy."Thymic Involution, Naive T Cell Decline, Inflammageing (IL-6, TNF, CRP), CMV, Vaccine Response ↓, High-Dose/Adjuvanted Vaccines (Flu HD/aQIV, Shingrix, PCV20, RSV)
Short Note"Immunology of pregnancy — tolerance mechanisms and drug safety."HLA-G/E, PD-L1, IDO, Tregs; SLE Flare/APS Management; HCQ/AZA Safe; MTX/LEF/MMF/CYC/JAKi Contraindicated; Certolizumab Safe; Anti-D Prophylaxis
Viva"Patient with septic shock day 5. mHLA-DR 20%. What does this mean and what therapies exist?"Immunoparalysis (mHLA-DR <30%); High Risk Secondary Infections; Investigational: IFN-γ, GM-CSF, IL-7; Supportive Care
Ward Round"Pregnant woman on adalimumab for Crohn's at 20 weeks. Management?"Continue Adalimumab until 20-24 Weeks, Then Stop; Certolizumab Safe Throughout; Plan Delivery/Pediatrician; Newborn: No Live Vaccines (BCG, Rotavirus) if Exposed 3rd Trimester
Last-Night"Ageing: Thymus Involution, Naive T↓, Inflammageing (IL-6/TNF/CRP), CMV↑, Vaccines: HD-Flu/aQIV, Shingrix, PCV20, RSV. Pregnancy: HLA-G/E/PD-L1/IDO/Treg. SLE Flare, APS LMWH+Aspirin, Certolizumab Safe, MTX/LEF/MMF/CYC/JAKi NO. RHD: Anti-D 28/34w + Post. Sepsis: Hyperinflam→Immunoparalysis (mHLA-DR<30%). Obesity: VAT→M1 Macs→TNF/IL-6→Insulin Resistance. Microbiome: SCFA→Treg, Dysbiosis→Disease. Vaccines: Live/Inact/Subunit/Conjugate/mRNA/Viral Vector. UK Schedule: 8/12/16w, 1y, 3y4m, 12-13y, 14y, ≥65. Hesitancy: 3Cs. Equity: Targeted Outreach."Compressed.

📌 Summary

  • Immunosenescence: Thymic Involution → ↓ Naive T Cells, ↑ Senescent/Memory T Cells, Inflammageing (Chronic IL-6, TNF, CRP), CMV Accelerates; Vaccine Response ↓ → High-Dose/Adjuvanted Vaccines (Fluzone HD, Fluad, Shingrix, PCV20, Arexvy/Abrysvo)
  • Pregnancy Immunology: Maternal-Fetal Tolerance (HLA-G, HLA-E, PD-L1, IDO, Tregs); Autoimmune Flare Risk (SLE 2nd/3rd Trimester); Drug Safety — Safe: HCQ, AZA, Certolizumab, IVIG; Contraindicated: MTX, LEF, MMF, CYC, JAKi, Rituximab (3rd Trimester); RHD Prophylaxis: Anti-D 28w/34w + Post-Delivery
  • Vaccines in Pregnancy: Tdap (16-32w), Influenza, COVID-19, RSV (28-36w) — All Inactivated/Non-Live; Live Vaccines Contraindicated
  • Critical Illness: Biphasic — Early Hyperinflammatory (Cytokine Storm) → Late Immunoparalysis (mHLA-DR <30%, Lymphopenia, PD-1↑, Tregs↑) → Secondary Infections; Experimental: IFN-γ, GM-CSF, IL-7
  • Obesity (Metaflammation): Visceral Adipose Tissue → M1 Macrophage Polarisation → TNF-α/IL-6/IL-1β → Insulin Resistance; Vaccine Response Impaired, ↑ Infection/Cancer/Autoimmunity Risk
  • Microbiome-Immune Axis: GALT (Peyer's Patches, M Cells, Lamina Propria LP); SCFAs → Treg ↑, Barrier Integrity ↑; Dysbiosis → IBD, RA, T1DM, MS, Obesity; Trained Immunity (BCG, β-Glucan → Epigenetic Reprogramming); FMT (rCDI >90% Cure)
  • Vaccinology: Platforms (Live Attenuated, Inactivated, Subunit, Conjugate, Viral Vector, mRNA, DNA, Protein Subunit); UK Schedule: 8/12/16w, 1y, 3y4m, 12-13y, 14y, ≥65y; Contraindications: Live Vaccines in Immunocompromised/Pregnancy; Hesitancy: 3 Cs (Confidence, Complacency, Convenience); Equity: Targeted Outreach
  • RHD: Anti-D Prophylaxis; Vaccines in Immunocompromised (No Live, Inactivated/Subunit/mRNA OK); Special Populations (Asplenia, CKD, HIV, Elderly)

❓ MCQs (10)

  1. Immunosenescence hallmark feature?

A. Thymic Hyperplasia B. Thymic Involution C. ↑ Naive T Cells D. ↓ Inflammatory Cytokines

Answer: B. Thymic Involution → ↓ Naive T Cell Output.

  1. Inflammageing — key cytokine?

A. IL-10 B. IL-6 C. IFN-γ D. IL-4

Answer: B. IL-6 (Also TNF-α, CRP) — Hallmark of Inflammageing.

  1. Pregnancy — which biologic is SAFE throughout?

A. Infliximab B. Adalimumab C. Certolizumab Pegol D. Rituximab

Answer: C. Certolizumab Pegol (PEGylated Fab', No Fc Transfer).

  1. Methotrexate in pregnancy — category?

A. Safe B. Contraindicated (Teratogenic) C. Safe 1st Trimester Only D. Safe 3rd Trimester Only

Answer: B. Contraindicated — Teratogenic (Category X).

  1. Rhesus Disease prevention — Anti-D timing?

A. 20w & 30w B. 28 Weeks & 34 Weeks + Post-Delivery C. 12w & 20w D. At Delivery Only

Answer: B. Routine Prophylaxis at 28w & 34w + Post-Delivery (Within 72h) + Sensitising Events.

  1. Sepsis immunoparalysis — best biomarker?

A. CRP B. PCT C. mHLA-DR on Monocytes <30% D. IL-6

Answer: C. mHLA-DR <30% on Monocytes = Immunoparalysis.

  1. Obesity & immunity — mechanism of insulin resistance?

A. ↑ Adiponectin B. VAT M1 Macrophages → TNF-α/IL-6 → IRS-1 Serine Phosphorylation C. ↑ Leptin Sensitivity D. ↓ TNF-α

Answer: B. VAT M1 Macrophages → TNF-α/IL-6 → JNK/IKKβ → IRS-1 Serine Phosphorylation.

  1. Trained Immunity — inducer?

A. Influenza Vaccine B. BCG Vaccine / β-Glucan C. Tetravalent Vaccine D. mRNA Vaccine

Answer: B. BCG, β-Glucan (Also Measles Vaccine).

  1. Pneumococcal vaccine for elderly — UK recommendation?

A. PPV23 Only B. PCV20 (Single Dose) OR PCV15 + PPV23 C. PCV13 Only D. PCV15 Only

Answer: B. PCV20 Single Dose OR PCV15 → PPV23 (1 Year Later).

  1. Vaccine hesitancy — 3 Cs?

A. Cost, Convenience, Compliance B. Confidence, Complacency, Convenience C. Culture, Community, Communication D. Cost, Coverage, Confidence

Answer: B. Confidence, Complacency, Convenience (WHO SAGE).

  1. FMT indication with highest evidence?

A. Obesity B. Recurrent C. difficile Infection (rCDI) C. Autism D. IBD

Answer: B. Recurrent C. difficile Infection (rCDI) — >90% Cure Rate.

  1. mRNA vaccine mechanism?

A. Enters Nucleus → Integrates DNA B. LNP-mRNA → Cytoplasm → Ribosome → Antigen → MHC I/II Presentation C. Viral Vector → DNA Integration D. Protein → Direct B Cell Activation

Answer: B. LNP-mRNA → Cytoplasm → Ribosome Translation → Antigen → MHC I/II Presentation.

📋 SBAs (10)

  1. 80F for flu vaccination. Best choice?

A. Standard Quadrivalent B. High-Dose (Fluzone HD) or Adjuvanted (Fluad) C. LAIV D. Any Answer: B.

  1. 32F on adalimumab for Crohn's, pregnant 10 weeks. Management?

A. Stop Immediately B. Continue Until 20-24 Weeks, Then Stop C. Switch to Certolizumab D. Increase Dose Answer: B.

  1. Septic patient Day 7. mHLA-DR 15%. Interpretation?

A. Hyperinflammatory B. Immunoparalysis C. Recovery D. Sepsis Resolved Answer: B.

  1. BMI 38 patient needs COVID booster. Expected response?

A. Normal B. Reduced (Impaired Antibody Titres, Faster Waning) C. Enhanced D. No Response Answer: B.

  1. Antibiotic-associated diarrhoea, recurrent C. difficile. Best treatment?

A. Vancomycin B. Fidaxomicin C. FMT (>90% Cure) D. Probiotics Answer: C.
